National Army 89

Has Advanced to Changting

| The Southern Route Army Will Attack Ruijin from Junmen |

Shantou Communication: The Eastern Route Army attacked Changting, and the Northern Route Army attacked *Shicheng, achieving successive victories in recent days. The main force of the bandits has been shaken, and their internal structure has collapsed, scattering and retreating southward. Previously, the bandits had built strong defensive fortifications in the mountains bordering Ting and Lian, and deployed defensive lines with Zhongwu Village as the first line, Nanshanba as the second line, Hetian as the third line, and the area outside Changting City along the Jinsha Creek Widow's Bridge as the fourth line. The Eastern Route Army recovered Zhongwu Village on the 29th. It is reported that more than 2,400 bandits were killed in this battle. On the 30th, the Eastern Route Army searched the highlands north and south of Huangyi and advanced towards the bandits' second line of defense, Nanshanba. The pseudo Fifth and Ninth Army Corps first camped on the northwest highlands, building trenches and minefields. Fighting began on the morning of the 4th, and by 2 PM, the National Army charged forward, killing more than 200 bandits from the pseudo 24th Division and capturing dozens of bandits. The remaining bandits retreated towards Hetian. Nanshanba is 12 li from Hetian and 50 li from Changting City, indicating that the Eastern Route Army has fully entered the territory of Ting. As for the Southern Route Army, it is now preparing to attack Ruijin, cutting off the bandits' retreat route southward. The National Army stationed in Junmen is reportedly already on the move. The bandits in Changting City are camped along the Ting River outside the city, occasionally scurrying to Dabagu Mu Village and Diaoyi, which are very close to Lanjia Ferry in Fengren City. The National Army stationed in Fengren City, Shanghang, consisting of the forces of Zeng Da-yu and Zhong Shao-kui, repelled the bandits in Diaoyi on the 5th. These bandits were the pseudo 24th Division, belonging to the pseudo Third Army Corps and the pseudo Fifth Army, who had fled from Nanshanba, numbering approximately 2,000. In recent days, in areas not far from the Southern Route Army's positions on the Fujian-Jiangxi border, such as Tanghu Da Shan, Mao Village's Bei Da Shan, and the Junmen Ridge area, many scattered bandits have been discovered, each group numbering between one and several hundred. Currently, the Huang Ren-huan Division is advancing northward towards Hangwu to search and suppress them. (August 8th)

A GlimPSE OF SOCIETY IN BEIPING 90

A Beggar Group Discovered in a Detoxification Center

A Red Actress Detained by the Puppet Government

Beiping Correspondence: Since the municipal government of Beiping vigorously implemented drug prohibition, two achievements have been most notable: 1) The Japanese Embassy has agreed that Korean nationals involved in drug trafficking will be punished entirely by Chinese law, which hopefully will eliminate the source of white powder in the future; 2) The detoxification center established by the municipal government has helped a large number of addicts to quit. Due to the center's well-equipped facilities and treatment, many addicts have been voluntarily reporting to the police stations and applying for admission. There have even been cases of entire families, including the elderly and young children, claiming to be addicted and willingly undergoing detoxification. According to the authorities at the center, as of today (the 10th), there have been more than ninety such petition-style family detoxification groups. The presence of such large groups of men, women, the old, and the young has suddenly transformed the atmosphere of the center, with noisy cries of children, resembling a bizarre exhibition of drug-addicted families. The authorities are urgently seeking remedies for this situation and have launched a thorough investigation. They have discovered a significant underlying issue: these so-called "voluntary detoxification" family groups are not actually addicted to drugs. Instead, they are families of impoverished people with no means of livelihood. They claim to be addicted to drugs due to hunger and cold, willing to impersonate drug offenders to get the "wowo tou" (cornbread) provided by the center for ten days a month, in order to prolong their family's near-starvation existence. After discovering this problem, the center's authorities, realizing that they could not accommodate so many disaster victims, have taken measures to send those already admitted to charitable organizations that provide relief to the starving. They have also revised the regulations, stipulating that anyone found to have falsely claimed addiction will be required to reimburse the cost of their food, clothing, lodging, and medicine, and will be sent to the Public Works and Public Security Bureaus for a short period of forced labor. This approach aims to provide relief to the starving while preventing fraudulent applications. However, the fact that good citizens are willing to falsely claim to be drug offenders and hope to be admitted to the detoxification center as a family reveals the extreme poverty of the lower strata of Beiping society, reaching a point of "one step away from death." This can be seen in the discovery of this dark reality. Beiping is the birthplace of "actresses." Since the government moved south, daughters from prominent families have abandoned their studies to learn acting. Not only descendants of the fallen Qing dynasty aristocracy, but even daughters of current university professors and city councilors, are openly learning acting and advertising themselves in newspapers, claiming to be raised by adoptive mothers. (Last year, Liang Jiayi, the district head of the Ping City Self-Government District, died in the hospital due to compulsory smoking cessation enforced by the city authorities. His daughter, Liang Yunqiu, told reporters that her father held a university teaching position and had a substantial income, so she could spend half her time learning acting without neglecting her studies. Now that her father had passed away and she was unable to continue her studies, she would use her skills to serve society and support her elderly mother, etc.). This is certainly due to economic reasons, but it also demonstrates that Beiping society generally recognizes acting as a shortcut to wealth. However, examining the past history of actresses, those who achieved great fame in Beiping, such as Liu Xikui, Xian Lingzhi, and Zhang Eyun, may have been fortunate on stage, but they all met with unfortunate ends in their personal lives. Recently, the famous Tsing Yi actress, Xue Yanqin (real name Huang Yongni), sold herself to Pu Gong, the younger brother of the puppet emperor, for 100,000 gold. While society has widely circulated stories about her building a luxurious residence in Dalian and visiting the traitor Pu in Changchun, and some even claimed that she was studying at the Tokyo School of Foreign Languages, attending classes with female students from various countries, including Europe, America, and Turkey, and behaving lavishly, socializing with Japanese noblewomen. In reality, Xue has been abandoned by Pu Gong and has long been in a difficult situation. According to news from Tianjin, Xue was abandoned by Pu Gong, who had recently become infatuated with a Japanese prostitute. Yesterday, she secretly fled to Tanggu and boarded the Japanese ship Changchun Maru. However, just as she was about to disembark, she was abducted by two Japanese soldiers and taken back to Dalian. Currently, the Huang residence in Beiping (the residence of Xue's parents in Beiping) has received a secret letter from the actress, pleading with her family to send someone to Changchun to rescue her. This can also serve as a lesson for those who "recognize a thief as a father." (10th)

Fujian Province 92

Implementing a Ban on Opium Poppy Cultivation

| The Provincial Government Announces Measures to Prohibit Cultivation |

Fuzhou Correspondence: Although Fujian Province has implemented a public monopoly on opium paste, with the Hubei Opium Prohibition Supervisory Office sending personnel to Fujian to establish offices and contract with merchants to organize companies to handle it by region, only opium from Sichuan, Yunnan, and Guizhou is sold. The cultivation of opium in Fujian Province is still strictly prohibited. The provincial government has now formulated measures to prohibit opium poppy cultivation and has issued an order to all administrative inspectors and commissioners to comply with it, in order to strengthen opium prohibition. The details are as follows:

(A) Before the opium poppies are sown: 1) Each administrative inspector and commissioner and county magistrate should issue and widely post notices, and distribute short notices stating that the cultivation of opium is strictly prohibited and violators will be executed, posting them in every village. 2) Each administrative inspector and commissioner should supervise the county magistrates to instruct the district offices to convene large meetings to prohibit opium cultivation, inviting representatives from various sectors of the Party, government, military, and education to attend. They should hold open-air lectures or organize propaganda teams to give lectures and prepare shoulder boards, sending people to beat gongs to promote the prohibition. County magistrates should personally attend the meetings in districts where opium cultivation has been more prevalent in the past. 3) Administrative inspectors and commissioners should supervise county magistrates to instruct district offices to order the heads of baojia (collective security units) to individually admonish each household and obtain written pledges stating "If I dare to plant opium, I will willingly accept the death penalty," and submit them to the county government for safekeeping. This may be waived in areas where it is deemed unnecessary to obtain pledges.

(B) When the opium is being sown: 1) Each administrative inspector and commissioner should issue an order to each county, instructing the district offices to supervise the heads of baojia to inspect the planting areas within their districts. If opium cultivation is discovered, the opium seeds should be immediately uprooted and the planters arrested and brought to justice. In districts where baojia heads have not yet been established, the district chiefs should be responsible for assigning people to conduct inspections. 2) District chiefs should regularly assess the diligence of all personnel under their jurisdiction and personally conduct inspections. Any officials who perform poorly should be reported to the county for punishment, and the inspection report should be submitted to the county for verification. 3) County magistrates should conduct spot checks on the situation in various districts, submit reports to the administrative inspectors and commissioners for verification, and forward them to the provincial government. District chiefs who fail to implement the measures effectively should be reported for punishment. 4) Administrative inspectors and commissioners should dispatch commissioners to conduct re-inspections in various counties. If county magistrates or military police are found to be shielding or condoning opium cultivation, they should immediately report it in secret to the commissioner's office and forward it to the provincial government for review and action.

(C) When the opium poppies sprout: 1) Each county magistrate should instruct the district offices to order the baojia heads to regularly survey the planting areas within their respective jurisdictions. If opium seedlings are discovered, they should immediately report it in secret to the district office for uprooting, and the planters should be arrested and brought to justice. In districts where baojia heads have not yet been established, the district chiefs should be responsible for handling the matter. 2) District chiefs should conduct occasional inspections in their respective districts

Page 11

and submit reports to the county for verification. If opium seedlings are discovered, they should be immediately eradicated, and the planters should be arrested and brought to justice, and the baojia heads should be reported to the county for punishment. 3) County magistrates should conduct spot checks on the handling of affairs in various districts, and first ascertain the period when opium seedlings in the county emerge and can be identified. They should report it to the administrative inspector and commissioner for verification and forwarding to the provincial government to determine the date for on-site inspection. The county magistrates should personally inspect each district. If opium seedlings are discovered, in addition to immediately supervising the police and militia to eradicate them and arrest the offenders for prosecution, they should also report the responsible officials at all levels for punishment. In areas bordering two or more counties, joint inspections should be conducted. 4) After the county magistrates have completed their inspections, the administrative inspectors and commissioners should, together with personnel dispatched by the provincial government, conduct re-inspections in various counties. If opium seedlings are discovered, in addition to supervising the eradication and severely punishing the planters, they should report the responsible county magistrates, district chiefs, and officials at all levels to the provincial government for punishment. 5) Administrative inspectors and commissioners may bring troops with them when inspecting and eradicating opium seedlings. 6) Administrative inspectors and commissioners may, when necessary, consult with the garrison troops for assistance or request the provincial government to send troops.

Hubei Province Again Abolishes Excessive Taxes and Levies 93

Sixty-four Types of Taxes Abolished in Thirty-nine Counties and Cities

Totaling One Million Yuan, Including Reductions in Land Tax

Hankou Correspondence: The Hubei Provincial Government, in accordance with a clear order from the Central Government, is thoroughly abolishing excessive local taxes and levies in order to reduce the burden on the people. The Department of Finance was tasked with planning the measures. In the first phase, twenty-seven types of excessive taxes and levies were abolished in seven cities, including Yichang, Shashi, Xinti, Wuxue, Laohekou, Fancheng, and Shayang, reducing the burden by over 280,000 yuan annually. This was implemented on July 1st. Subsequently, due to severe floods and droughts, excessive taxes and levies in other counties have not been completely abolished, and the people are increasingly unable to bear the burden. The provincial government then ordered the Department of Finance to plan a second phase of abolishing excessive taxes and levies. This has now been finalized. The items to be abolished include: In the First Administrative District, Puqi: special tea merchant tax, fish industry shop tax, hemp industry shop tax; Hanyang: bamboo and timber tax, door tax, house tax; Caidian: business contribution, fish fry dike tax; Jiayu: public security miscellaneous tax, flower, hemp, silk, and bean tax; Xianning: special business tax, business education tax, boat household public security tax, tea, hemp, and paper business tax. In the Second Administrative District, Yangxin: inn tax, salt and grass tax; Daye: flower and hemp business tax, lime tax. In the Third Administrative District, Qichun: grain export registration fee, local specialty tax, cotton and hemp tax, river tax; Xishui: public welfare business tax; Huangmei: paper money tax, brewing tax. In the Fourth Administrative District, Huangpi: public security business tax, wheel tax; Lishan: oil pressing tax. In the Fifth Administrative District, Xiaogan: public security business tax; Yingcheng: public welfare tax. In the Sixth Administrative District, Tianmen: door tax; Hanchuan: water police miscellaneous tax; Mianyang: silk, flower, and egg tax. In the Seventh Administrative District, Jiangling: salt jin surcharge; Songzi: cotton tax, naked stone tax, tobacco and alcohol tax, oil pressing tax, miscellaneous grain tax; Jianli: bamboo and timber tax, flower package tax. In the Eighth Administrative District, Yicheng: door grain cotton tax; Guanghua: oil pressing industry tax, cotton ginning tax; Gucheng: business shop surcharge; Baokang: lodging tax. In the Ninth Administrative District, Yuan'an: paper trough tax, public welfare tax; Yidu: entertainer tax; Xingshan: salt merchant shop tax, almanac tax; Zigui: special export goods tax, salt tax, military reception fee, special goods public welfare tax, aviation patriotic contribution; Wufeng: salt tax, timber tax, lacquer knife tax, tea tax, tung oil tax, paper trough tax; Changyang: household tax, paper trough tax. In the Tenth Administrative District, Xuan'en: security monthly contribution; Badong: almanac tax; Hefeng: business protection tax, lacquer tax, tea tax; Lichuan: intermediary tax; Xianfeng: market business tax; Laifeng: grass tobacco tax. In the Eleventh Administrative District, Junxian: public security tax, incense tax, tobacco leaf tax, tung oil tax; Yunxi: salt brokerage tax, inn tax; Zhushan: temporary military transport tax, salt boat tax, cotton tax; Zhuxi: tobacco and alcohol tax; Wuxue: salt merchant assistance donation, wharf tax. The above totals sixty-four types of taxes and levies in thirty-nine counties and one city, amounting to 452,198 yuan. These funds were originally used for education, security, county administration, baojia, police administration, new construction, and various military service supplies, but they have all been completely abolished. As for the reduction in land tax surcharges, they include: Wuchang field mu donation, Xianning field mu donation, Echeng field mu donation, Xishui land tax surcharge county administration and education donations, Huangmei land tax surcharge education donation, Guangji field mu donation, Luotian ticket surtax school donation, Macheng field mu donation, Hanchuan field mu donation, Shishou field mu surcharge education donation, Baokang field mu surcharge, Dangyang field mu surcharge, Xingshan land tax surtax education donation, Zigui property securities, land tax post-war donation, Dingtun surtax school donation, Dingtun surtax public security donation, Jianshi field mu donation, Badong ticket surtax county administration donation, Laifeng ticket surtax school donation, Junxian ticket surtax collection fee, Fangxian ticket surtax collection fee, Zhushan advance grain county administration donation, advance mu donation, Zhuxi field mu surcharge, land tax surtax administrative fee, totaling twenty-one counties, reducing revenue by 520,221 yuan. (12th)

Inspection Tour of Northwest China 94

By Our Special Correspondent, Geng Ya

The Ta'er Monastery, Birthplace of the Founder of Yellow Sect Buddhism (Part II)

The Lesser Golden Tile Temple has two stories and contains Buddhist statues that are grotesque and terrifying, along with an assortment of ancient hunting implements such as bows and arrows, spears and halberds, spiked maces, knives and guns, ferocious masks, iron chain armor, etc., as well as specimens of lions, tigers, bears, leopards, apes, wild oxen, and other wild beasts. Worshippers splatter butter oil all over the Buddhist statues and specimens and stick copper coins on them, creating an unpleasant, greasy smell. Only the roof tiles, said to be the same as those of the Great Golden Tile Temple, are made of copper and gilded, with a gleaming golden color that reflects and complements each other, making them the monastery's most dazzling adornments.

"Da Jin Wa" (transliteration) is the residence of the Living Buddha, distributed east and west with a total of sixteen courtyards. Banners are erected in front of the gates, towering into the sky. The "Chop Altar Tree" (transliteration) grows next to the Great Golden Tile Temple. Legend says that when Tsongkhapa was born, his blood spilled on the ground, and this tree grew from it. The trunk is like a peach tree, with transparent bark that reveals textures resembling Tibetan script. It is also said that in ancient times, a small Living Buddha could often be seen sitting on the leaves of the tree on Mid-Autumn Night. There are many similar mystical anecdotes associated with the monastery. The kitchen of the Great Golden Tile Temple contains three large iron pots, each measuring one square zhang (approximately 3.3 meters). Each pot can hold enough to cook nine cows. The walls are lined with thousands of tea bowls, used for cooking tea and rice during major gatherings. When the food is cooked, the cooks first tie iron ropes around their waists, securing the other end to a pillar, and then use long ladles to scoop out the food, frequently removing it, to prevent accidentally falling into the pot and becoming cooked themselves. Other halls contain strange statues of different genders embracing each other, some between humans, some between humans and beasts, and some with beast-like demons. Considering their forms and contemplating their intentions, they are similar to the Joyful Buddha. They are all intriguing and inexplicable.

The largest annual event is the Buddha Display Festival, held on the seventh day of the sixth month of the lunar calendar. In the morning, an image of Tsongkhapa is carried out and displayed on the hillside, with a solemn chanting ceremony. Tibetan people flock to the gathering in groups of thousands, some prostrating themselves under the image and others worshipping from afar. Finally, everyone throws silver coins at the Buddha image. The merchants who set up stalls on the spot pay heavy rent, making it a major source of income for the monastery. In the afternoon, images of Arhats, Dharma Protectors, and others are dressed up and dance in turn in the Shehuo (community fire) courtyard. Afterward, a triangular wooden tray is used to carry a dough figurine, which is cleaved and sent out, said to be a ritual related to Nian Gengyao killing a Living Buddha. The lamas hate him and fear his reincarnation, so they use Buddhist practices to suppress him. At night, the drums and music are deafening, and visitors are prohibited from watching. It is suspected that the ritual is a ceremony to shoot the image of Nian Gengyao.

The number of lamas and monks was 3,500 twenty years ago, but is now about 2,500. Their organization is roughly divided into the following departments: 1) The Great Dharma Master, who explains Buddhist scriptures, manages the Living Buddhas, and oversees all the affairs of the monastery; 2) The Great Monk Manager, who manages the monks; 3) The First Elder, who is responsible for internal affairs; 4) The Second Elder, who is responsible for foreign affairs and handles the litigation affairs of the Tibetan people in the administered area; 5) The Third Elder, who manages revenue and expenditure; 6) The Buddha Presider, who protects the scripture hall. All are elected to serve rotating terms. The remaining lamas have no rank. They chant scriptures three times a day, or only once if they have official duties. Living Buddha is the Chinese term for lama. After death, the destination of their reincarnation is divined by other Living Buddhas. (In reality, this is often inaccurate, and wealthy families secretly bribe to have their sons selected as Living Buddhas.) At the age of eight or nine, they are welcomed back to the monastery and taught the scriptures by the Great Dharma Master. If a young Living Buddha commits a violation, the Great Dharma Master can reprimand him with a leather whip, but he must bow to him afterward. The other ordinary lamas are called monks. Some are initially sent by the people, providing their own monastic robes and presenting a hada (silk scarf) to the Great Dharma Master and their master. Others who return from other monasteries only present two hundred copper coins, which are returned to them when they leave. If they revert to secular life, they receive nothing. The monastery has over thirty large and small Living Buddhas, living a life of comfort and luxury, like nobles. The thousands of other monks are each provided with only two dou (approx. 20 liters) and one sheng (approx. 1 liter) of grain per year, so they must beg for alms and seek help from relatives. Some even engage in business and lending to make ends meet. Their staple food is tsampa (roasted barley flour) fried with butter oil. They wear robes and aprons and go barefoot without pants. Some wear leather boots. They only wear hats when chanting scriptures.

For funerals, if it is for a monk or an ordinary Living Buddha, they still use the water, fire, or sky burial methods used by the Tibetan people. If it is for a high-ranking and wealthy Living Buddha with private property, the body is dissected, the intestines are removed, and mercury is poured in, or salt mud is applied and changed every few days. The blood that flows out is mixed with white clay, kneaded into balls, and placed in a talismanic Buddha, which is worn for protection, believing it can ward off guns and cannons. The corpse is then cured into jerky, then the dissected area is sewn up, the body is dressed in robes, and gold is applied to the face. It is placed in a gold-inlaid glass niche and displayed in the scripture hall in order, called the gold body of the nth reincarnation of so-and-so Living Buddha.

The monastery's wealth was once said to be enough to pay off the Boxer Indemnity. It is said that during the National Army's garrison in Gansu, a general visited the monastery and stared at the golden tiles for a long time without blinking. The lamas suspected him and quickly raised 300,000 gold, which they presented to the general in cooperation with a Tibetan prince with close ties. The truth is difficult to ascertain, but the 143 monasteries in Qinghai annually support hundreds of thousands of non-productive, leisurely Tibetan monks. Just the cost of three meals a day is considerable. If political means could be used to transfer this wealth to the education and animal husbandry of the Tibetan people, it would passively eliminate superstition and actively increase production. From then on, the national life of the Tibetan people would suddenly erupt with astonishing and world-shaking light.

National Goods Inspection Tour of the Yangtze River 95

(IV) Constant

Nanchang has long been known as a land of fish and rice. In the past, it suffered greatly from banditry. The people were displaced and their homes were destroyed. Now that the military operations are coming to an end, the province hopes to recover its vitality in a few years through comprehensive construction. However, after this great disaster, the phenomenon of economic decline is worrying. We can understand its general situation by observing its industries. In Jingdezhen, there used to be 3,000 kilns with one million workers, producing 60 to 70 million taels of porcelain annually. In 1928, there were still 130 kilns with 200,000 to 300,000 workers. Recent investigations show that the annual output is no more than 3 million yuan, and exports to overseas are no more than 70,000 to 80,000 dan (approx. 3.5-4 tons). The tragic decline has led to the complete failure of China's entire porcelain industry, which is truly heartbreaking. Jiangxi's tea has always been famous. In 1928, exports were still over 160,000 dan, but by 1932, it was only 80,000 dan. Jiangxi's paper also occupies a position in China's paper industry. The province produces 6 million yuan worth of paper, most of which is consumed domestically. However, most of the paper consumed in the country is still foreign. Whether Jiangxi's paper can stand firm depends on whether it can be improved and progress. Ramie cloth is a specialty of Jiangxi. According to investigations, in the most prosperous years, the output was 600,000 dan. According to exports from Jiujiang Customs in 1931, it has fallen to just over 70,000 dan, indicating a significant reduction in output. Pingsiang's coal reserves are estimated at 200 trillion tons, and Jiangxi produces tungsten ore, a world-renowned metal, accounting for 50% of the world's production, ranking first in the world. In the years with the most exports, it amounted to 140,000 dan, worth 6 million yuan. In 1932, exports decreased to just over 30,000 dan, worth 800,000 yuan. However, in the event of war in the world, it will still be an important material. Jiangxi's rice used to produce an average of 6.5 million shi (approx. 650,000 tons) annually. After deducting the consumption of the province's population, about 2.5 million shi could be used to supplement the needs of other provinces. However, recently, there have still been imports of rice from other provinces and foreign countries, because agricultural production has decreased, and the military's consumption is large, resulting in insufficient food self-sufficiency in the province. The above is the general situation of Jiangxi's industries. We can also get a glimpse of Jiangxi's economic situation from the import and export statistics of Jiujiang Customs. In 1932, exports were 13,429,599 taels, and imports were 23,599,206 taels, resulting in a trade deficit of over 10 million taels. The reason for the trade deficit is the banditry in the province, which has reduced production. At the same time, the consumption of a large military force has increased the volume of imports. However, what helps to offset this is that hundreds of millions of yuan in military pay are distributed in the market every month, allowing financial circulation. In the future, when the troops withdraw and the bargaining chips decrease, there will be no way to offset the deficit. The wealth of the people will decline, and their purchasing power will weaken. If plans are not made early, the trade deficit will likely increase, and the economic situation will become even more unbearable. The best news we obtained in Nanchang is that Mr. Du Chongyuan is establishing a large-scale porcelain factory. Mr. Lin recently returned from an inspection in Jingdezhen and believes that if political forces can assist, the porcelain industry has the potential for revival. Furthermore, the Jiangxi Provincial Government, recognizing the importance of agricultural production, has recently organized an Agricultural Institute to integrate the province's agricultural administration, education, and technology under its command, with guaranteed independent funding. It advocates integrating agricultural technology with rural construction, which is truly good news for farmers in the province.

The highways that have been opened to traffic in Nanchang include the Gan-Zhejiang, Gan-Hunan, and Gan-Guangdong routes. In addition, what can promote Nanchang's prosperity is the construction of the Gan-Zhejiang and Gan-Hunan railways, which connect to the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway to the east and the Zhuping Railway to the west. The completion of these two routes will have a huge impact on national defense and commerce. In particular, the commercial and economic value will be even greater. At present, Jiangxi's products rely solely on Jiujiang for transportation. Inland transportation relies on porters and boats, and traffic on the Yangtze River is also slow. With the opening of the Gan-Zhejiang route, the province's products can be concentrated in Nanchang, transported to Hangzhou, and then shipped overseas. The freight costs for rice, porcelain, tea, and Pingsiang coal will be greatly reduced, making it easier to promote commercial prosperity.

The Nanchang exhibition concluded on September 27th, and we returned to Jiujiang. Jiujiang has a population of 70,000 and is a distribution center for goods in Jiangxi. Although it is the end point of the Nanxun Railway, it is only a transfer port. There are few people with consumption power, so it is not easy to revitalize commerce. If the Gan-Zhejiang and Gan-Hunan railways are opened, inland goods will abandon waterways and use land routes, further impacting Jiujiang. It can only hope to find a way out in industrial manufacturing to reverse the decline. Jiujiang has the Jiuxing Textile Company. It is most suitable to set up a porcelain factory in Jiujiang, because it is close to the kaolin clay production area in Xingzi County, making it convenient to obtain materials. The impression of Japanese goods in Jiujiang is not as good as in Nanchang. In order to adapt to the environment, our group shortened the exhibition period by three days and screened the film "China's Silk" for various schools to promote production education. This initiative was well received by the student community. The exhibition period ended on October 4th. Then, we prepared to go to Hankou.

Songjiang 96

Villagers in Xiajiang Township Obstruct Land Survey

Our county's land survey work began in the old tenth district and has already been completed. However, yesterday, Zhang Zishan, a surveyor from Xiazhuang Township, was suddenly attacked by dozens of villagers while working. The villagers beat the surveyor and took away the measuring rods and tapes. He Xuzu, the leader of the survey team at the location, believed that the villagers were unreasonable and had no choice but to temporarily retreat to avoid confrontation. He reported the situation to the Land Bureau Preparation Office, which forwarded it to the county government for prompt action.

Suzhou 97

Gamblers Resist Arrest, Assault Police

In Suzhou, every late autumn traditionally involves cricket fighting for gambling. This autumn, due to strict crackdowns by the authorities, crowds are gathering at Jiangdun Village in the Xiangshan area by Taihu Lake to gamble on cricket fights. Many people from neighboring counties also bring crickets to fight, with substantial sums changing hands. On the afternoon of the twelfth, Qin Zhude, a patrol officer from the Guangfu Eighth Precinct, learned of this. That evening, he led his entire shift of police officers to surround Jiangdun Village and make arrests. Unexpectedly, the gamblers resisted as a group, and the police were instead surrounded and violently attacked. As a result, in addition to Qin Zhu being injured in the assault, two other police officers sustained severe injuries and are in critical condition. The village chief Jiang Yijing and a gambling ringleader, surnamed Yang, were subsequently apprehended and escorted to the city on the afternoon of the thirteenth. The injured police officers have been sent to the hospital for treatment.

Dr. Yuan Boying Relocates to Suzhou for Practice 98

Dr. Yuan Boying of Huata is an expert in venereal and skin diseases, with expertise passed down through four generations. He inherited the family's knowledge and possesses secretly prepared internal and external medicines known for their remarkable efficacy. Due to the remoteness and inconvenience of his rural residence, and for the convenience of patients, he has relocated to No. 33, Inside the Shikumen Gate, Wu Ya Chang Brick Bridge, inside Fengmen city, Suzhou, and has already begun seeing patients.

Wuxi 99

Thugs Rob and Kill on the Spot

Lu Weiji, the 48-year-old owner of the Feixia Pavilion teahouse in Xin Sanli Bridge outside the North Gate, has a son and a daughter. The previous evening (the twelfth) around 9 p.m., his daughter, Ji Ying, was carrying her three-year-old younger brother, Sanbao, to the Song Mao Xiang tea shop at the Lao Sanli Bridge to buy tea. Unexpectedly, when they reached the vicinity of Lu Youfeng Lane, they were suddenly confronted by a thug who blocked their way and forcibly snatched the silver anklet from Sanbao's right foot. Ji Ying shouted for help, and passersby, hearing the cry, rushed to apprehend the thief. They managed to capture the thug and severely beat him, resulting in his death amidst the chaos. Afterwards, Wu Qiao Second Police Station of the Fifth Public Security Bureau apprehended a suspect, Ji Luo Zhou, and took him to the station for interrogation. Meanwhile, Bureau member Gu Songxun summoned the Lu family, father and daughter, for questioning. Yesterday morning (the thirteenth) at 9 a.m., Wu Changgen, the Tutouzheng of Tian Si Tu, reported the incident to the local branch of the District Court, requesting an autopsy. The investigating judge, along with Wang, the coroner, proceeded to conduct the autopsy and confirmed that the man had died from the beating. The Tutouzheng was instructed to prepare a coffin for burial, and the suspect was taken to the court for interrogation. It is reported that the deceased was named Xi A Quan, approximately 20 years old, and was a prostitute, who resorted to this desperate measure, resulting in his being beaten to death.

Hua Juchu, County Clerk, Detained 100

Hua Juchu, the chief of general affairs at the local tobacco and alcohol public sales and excise office, was found to be addicted to opium. He had not registered with the county's anti-opium society. He was reported by a vendor, Wang Zuogeng, and taken to the First Precinct, then transferred to the county's anti-opium society. Yu Quanqing, a clerk, interrogated him. Hua Juchu insisted that he had indeed used opium in the past but had now quit. However, Wang Zuogeng claimed that Hua was a long-time addict of more than twenty years. Their statements conflicted. The court ordered Wang Zuogeng to post bail, while County Magistrate Yan personally instructed Police Chief Wu to keep Hua Juchu under strict surveillance, forbidding anyone from visiting him. Yesterday, he was sent to the rehabilitation center for examination. If the county's examination proves inconclusive, he will be sent to the provincial capital for further examination before a final decision is made.

Changshu 101

First Trial Run on the Xichang Highway Results in Overturn

The Xichang Highway, connecting this county and Wuxi, was ordered to be built and has been completed for some time. However, on the side of our county, there are several missing water gullies and soil foundations of bridge piers which have not yet been filled. Therefore, last time, Wang Xiaolai and others, the initiators of the Shanghai-Wuxi Automobile Company, planned to inspect the road from Wuxi to Changshu, but it did not happen because the roadbed was not yet compacted. Now, the Xihu Road Engineering Office received an order from the Construction Department that the Xichang section should be opened to traffic within this month. Therefore, Sun Wei'e, the head of the first section of the road, accompanied by the construction technician and others, totaling seven people, drove a bridge-laying vehicle from Wuxi to Changshu on the twelfth for a trial run. The vehicle also carried pine planks to bridge the water gullies. However, the road had not been rolled and was uneven, making the ride very unstable, especially in the Changshu section. At about 6 p.m. that day, the vehicle reached the Wengjia Village area of Yangjian in this county. Because it was already dusk, they encountered a large water gully, causing the vehicle to suddenly overturn. All the contents of the vehicle were scattered on the ground. Fortunately, the technician and engineers were unharmed. They, along with the villagers, helped to right the vehicle and spent the night in Wengjia Village. They continued driving to Changshu on the morning of the thirteenth.

Changzhou 102

Bandits Rob and Injure

Zhu Yinsheng, a brick bridge worker from Liyang, walked from Benniu to Changzhou on the evening of the twelfth, intending to take a car to Shanghai to seek a livelihood. When he was walking through the Lushen Hou Tangshen Port area along the railway outside the North Gate, he suddenly encountered seven or eight bandits armed with guns, who shouted at him to stop. They stepped forward to search Zhu's person. At that time, it was not yet late, and there were pedestrians coming and going. Fearing that he would raise the alarm, the bandits pulled out a pistol and aimed it at Zhu's head, shooting him. Zhu immediately fell to the ground, two front teeth were knocked out, and blood flowed freely. All the seventeen yuan he had hidden and a bag of clothes were robbed. Afterwards, the nearby police station learned of the incident and sent police to send him to Wujin Hospital for treatment. The bullet entered from the back of his head and exited from his mouth. According to the doctor, his life may be saved.

Large parade and camp of Boy Scouts of the Third District of this province. Haimen 104

Landlord Forces Tenant Farmer to Death

Huang Guilang, a farmer from Gongjia Town in the Sixth District, is from a impoverished family. This year, he rented one thousand mu of land from landlord Chen Laoer. Due to the prolonged drought, the cotton and grain harvests were poor, yielding very little. The other day, Chen demanded rent from Huang. Huang was unable to pay and pleaded for a reduction or exemption. Chen refused and vehemently insulted and berated him. Eventually, with the mediation of neighbors, they agreed that it be paid in full by the twentieth of this month. Chen reluctantly left. Huang, deeply affected by this, felt extremely resentful and developed suicidal thoughts. Yesterday evening, he hanged himself. By the time his family discovered it and tried to save him, he was already dead.

Verdict in the Case of Throwing a Girl to Death 105

Huang Hexiang, a farmer from Zhengyun Township in the Second District of Qidong, married Yuan Fuliang's daughter, Genzhu, from the same village in the spring of the year before last. Since their marriage, their relationship had been poor, and they often quarreled. In July of this year, she gave birth to a daughter, who was then thrown to death by Hexiang. Yuan Fuliang filed a complaint with the county government, and Yang, the judge, went to examine the body, arrested and detained Huang Hexiang. After several interrogations, the plaintiff and witnesses all testified that Huang Hexiang had indeed thrown the girl to death. The other day, Judge Yang sentenced Huang Hexiang to ten years of imprisonment according to the crime of murder.

Jiaxing 109

County Disaster Relief Committee Established

The Jiaxing County Disaster Relief Committee held its inaugural meeting the other day and decided on the following: (1) Use the original site of the insect control association as the office; (2) All members of the committee are responsible for fundraising, and Yao Mulian and Fang Qingxiang are publicly elected as fundraising committee members; (3) Send a letter to the county government to allocate all the funds for insect control to disaster relief expenses; (4) The county's grain stabilization matters will also be planned and handled by the committee.

Jiaxing Bank Declares Closure 110

Jiaxing Commercial Bank is a limited liability company with a capital of 250,000 yuan. The shareholders include Jiang Lanxian and Gao Zhonglan, among others. It has been in operation for more than ten years. In the past, it enjoyed a good reputation in the business community. The bank also established a savings department to handle various savings accounts, attracting a significant amount of cash deposits, especially zero-deposit lump-sum payments and fixed-term savings. However, after the Ziyuan, Juyuan, and Hengyuan money shops closed on September 30, the bank was also affected by the withdrawals of depositors. On the morning of the thirteenth, it announced its closure. Before closing, it posted a public announcement stating: "This bank is temporarily suspending receipts and payments due to market influences. The bank will convene a shareholders' meeting of directors to determine further measures." However, depositors believed that savings deposits should be accounted for separately and that the bank should bear unlimited liability. Therefore, they would form a creditors' group to demand full repayment of principal and interest from the responsible parties of the bank.

Onboard Nagasaki Maru to Japan and then to Russia

No Special Mission this time

Shanghai-Guangdong Line, Dolphin Aircraft Test Flight 113

Returned to Beijing and Shanghai yesterday afternoon

Reception in the afternoon for all sectors to fly around the city

The Shanghai-Guangdong flight will be officially resumed on the 2nd of next month

The Shenshi News Agency reports that the China Aviation Corporation's Douglas new aircraft on the Shanghai-Guangdong line conducted a long-distance test flight between Beijing and Shanghai yesterday. Zhu Jia-hua, Minister of Transportation, came to Shanghai to inspect. In the afternoon, people from all walks of life were invited to fly around the city, and the results were satisfactory. It has been decided to resume the flight on the 2nd of next month. The details are as follows:

Implement Long-Distance Test Flights Between Beijing and Shanghai 114

After the China Aviation Corporation's new aircraft was tested at Longhua for several days, Ericson drove the aircraft from Shanghai to Beijing at 11 am yesterday for the first long-distance flight. The flight took one hour and five minutes, and it arrived safely at Minggugong Airport in Nanjing at 12:05. Zhu Jiahua, Minister of Communications, took the plane from Beijing at 12:30 to return to Shanghai to inspect everything. He returned safely to Longhua at 1:30 pm, which only took two and a half hours for the round trip. The results were good, and Zhu Jiahua, Minister of Communications, was quite satisfied.

Invite All Sectors to Fly Around the City 115

The China Aviation Corporation invited people from all walks of life in this port to take a flight around the city starting at 3:30 pm yesterday. Dozens of Chinese and foreign guests attended, and they were received by Dai Enji, the manager of the China Aviation Corporation, and Huang Baoxian and He Jingzhi, the directors of the business department. A total of five batches of test flights were conducted, and each circled the city for a week, taking about fifteen minutes. When flying at a height of two thousand feet, the scenery of the whole city can be seen at a glance from below the plane. The Suzhou River, which is as thin as a ditch, and the street houses, which are as detailed as tiles, have all changed their original shapes and are like children's toys. It was not until 5:30 pm that it was completed. After each guest had some refreshments, they returned happily.

Officially Resumed on the 2nd of Next Month 116

Yesterday, the company officially announced that the Shanghai-Guangdong line has been decided to resume operations from the 2nd of next month. It is tentatively scheduled to run once a week to and from. From December, it will be increased to twice a week to and from. In the first month of resumption, passengers will not be carried temporarily, only mail. In order to ensure flight safety, the China Aviation Corporation's wireless stations at each station on the Shanghai-Guangdong line have been providing detailed weather reports every day in the past few months. The wireless station recently established on Tanxu Island in Hangzhou has been completed. Therefore, in the future, during the opening period, carrying passengers and transporting mail can have extremely safe guarantees.

Shanghai-Guangdong Flight Schedule Set 117

The round-trip flight schedule of the Shanghai-Guangdong route after the resumption of service has been tentatively set as follows: (1) The southbound flight departs from Shanghai at 6:00 am every Friday, leaves Wenzhou at 8:00 am, leaves Fuzhou at 10:25 am, leaves Xiamen at 11:55 am, leaves Shantou at 1:15 pm, and arrives in Guangzhou at 3:00 pm. (2) The northbound flight leaves Guangzhou at 6:30 am, leaves Shantou at 8:35 am, leaves Xiamen at 9:55 am, leaves Fuzhou at 11:25 am, leaves Wenzhou at 1:05 pm, and arrives in Shanghai at 3:00 pm. From December 1, it will be changed to two round trips per week. The southbound flight departs from Shanghai every Tuesday and Friday, and the northbound flight departs from Guangzhou every Thursday and Sunday. The schedule is the same as above.

Famine Relief Association for Droughts in Various Provinces 118

Inaugural Meeting Today

Initiated by Minister Kong and Xu Shiying

Meeting held at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce at 4 pm

The Shijie News Agency reports that since the beginning of the summer of this year, Finance Minister Kong Xiangxi and Xu Shiying, the Chairman of the National Relief Committee, have been suffering from drought, with no rain for three months. More than ten provinces have been affected by the disaster, and the disaster victims have exceeded hundreds of thousands. If relief is not provided urgently, the severe winter will be approaching in a blink of an eye, and the disaster victims will have no food or clothing. It is very pitiful. Therefore, it has united leaders from all walks of life, such as Du Yuesheng, Wang Yiting, Zhang Xiaolin, Wen Lanting, Wang Xiaolai, Yu Qiaqing, etc., to initiate the organization of the Shanghai Fundraising Famine Relief Association for Droughts in Various Provinces to appeal for the victims. It has been soliciting enthusiastic people from all walks of life to join for days, and preparations have been completed. The inaugural meeting has been scheduled for today (Sunday) at 4 pm in the auditorium of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce at Tianhougong Bridge. All initiators have been notified to attend at that time to jointly plan the proceedings so that the dying disaster victims can have some hope of recovery.

Various Groups 119

Important News on Fundraising for Drought Relief

Xinwei Relief Association: Yesterday, it received a telegram from the Aftermath Committee for Droughts in Yuqian County, Zhejiang Province, begging for relief. The telegram said, "Our county has suffered repeated crop failures, and the vitality of farmers' livelihoods has been hurt, almost falling into despair. Now, it has suffered from drought again, affecting the entire county. According to the survey, the autumn harvest is less than 20%, and the food loss is 200,000 dan. More than 42,000 of the 63,000 people in the county are in a state of being unable to cook without rice. The plight of the victims is unspeakable. The members of our association do not dare to be presumptuous, and dare to specially beg for the lives of tens of thousands of victims. We respectfully request that your association send personnel to conduct an on-site survey and allocate funds for relief. We are extremely grateful."

Hubei Fellow Association: The fundraising association received a letter from Ouyang Honglie, the magistrate of Xiaogan County, stating that the county has an area of ​​about 13,300 square li and a population of more than 698,000 people. The disaster-stricken area is actually about 220 li long and about 310 li long. The number of victims is about 510,000. Except for those who have fled, there are currently about 470,000 people waiting for relief. The severity of the drought is rarely seen in decades. In addition, Li Jiying, the magistrate of Jiayu County, telegraphed on behalf of the county, stating that the county covers an area of ​​15,000 square li and has a population of 161,032 people. The county's drought-stricken farmland is about 110,000 mu, and the number of victims reaches 114,000. Because the government prohibits cross-border begging, there are still few who have fled. About 93,000 people are waiting for relief. In addition, Sun Yezhen, the magistrate of Lishan County, telegraphed that the county covers an area of ​​about 11,330 square li and has a population of 267,809 people. The area of ​​farmland affected by the three disasters of water, drought, and bandits is about 150,000 mu, and the number of victims is about 90,000. In addition, Yang Shisheng, the magistrate of Wuchang County, said in a letter that the drought in the county is extremely severe. According to statistics, the disaster area accounts for eight-tenths of the entire county, with a total population of 369,361, and as many as 263,527 people affected. This kind of holocaust is really only seen in history.

Huining Fellow Association: The disaster relief committee convened the third standing committee meeting on the 12th, with Mr. Tang Zhi presiding and Wang Yisan recording. First, the chairman reported, and the disaster reports and telegrams from the counties belonging to the two prefectures were completed, and the following proposals were discussed and decided: (1) Send a letter to the China Foreign Famine Relief Association for relief, and learn that Mr. Becker of the association has gone to Wuhu in Huining to investigate the disaster situation. In addition to sending telegrams to Commissioner Zhou of the Ninth District, Commissioner Liu of the Tenth District, and local gentry, etc., to properly receive them, also send appropriate personnel to accompany them to conduct on-site inspections of the disaster area to show the severity of the disaster. (2) A previous letter to the Huining Hall in this city requesting assistance in relief has not yet been responded to. Reiterate the previous case and provide further requirements detailing the tragic situation in each disaster area, and request a reply as soon as possible. (3) The disaster situation in each county is dire, and the victims are waiting for relief. It is urgent to save them from displacement. In order to seek emergency relief, send a letter to the Huining Fellow Association in Shanghai, and forward a letter to the fellow associations in each county, immediately allocating the balance of funds for grain stabilization in their hometowns in 1911 to the association for disaster relief to meet emergency needs. (4) Reports from each county are as numerous as snowflakes and should be summarized and published in newspapers every day to promote publicity. (5) Publish advertisements in local newspapers in this city soliciting relief. (6) Recommend Tang Zhixian and Cao Zhigong to represent the association and participate in the inaugural meeting of the Shanghai Fundraising Famine Relief Association for Droughts in Various Provinces. (7) Recommend Xu Jiyu, Yang Xiaotian, Wang Dizhang, Tang Zhixian, Cao Zhigong, and other five gentlemen to represent the association and personally ask for relief from various charitable organizations in this city to maximize results. (8) Distribute donation books immediately and widely solicit donations from fellow associations inside and outside the port, collect donations from all sides, and engage in relief.

The meeting was adjourned after discussing and carrying out various fundraising methods.

International Radio Station Continues to Test International Calls 121

Once Prepared

It can be Officially Called

The Central News Agency reports that the International Radio Station of the Ministry of Communications tested calls with Britain, Germany, the United States, and France last winter, and submitted the results of the test to the Ministry of Communications for active preparation. Relief to the Silk Industry 122

According to Director He, a reporter said that the government has provided relief to the silk industry many times, but the results have been minimal due to poor methods. Now that the world economy is in decline, my country's silk industry is becoming more and more depressed. Moreover, opinions are divided, and it cannot be decided in the short term. Mr. He also expressed that the current method will be tailored to the requirements of both silk and silk parties as much as possible, and both parties must strictly abide by it in order to completely solve the problem.

Your bank's ability to rein in at the precipice and suddenly realize is sincerely gratifying to us. Even with a verbal declaration of cessation, the association believes that it is not enough to demonstrate credibility to the Chinese people. The association, as it is responsible for opposing loans, hereby proposes the following three points: (1) Issue a letter to Desai Company in the name of your bank, declaring the permanent cessation of loans. This letter must be inspected by the association. (2) Your bank should immediately recall the loan contract, convene various mass organizations and the press in Shanghai, and destroy the original loan contract in public. (3) Your bank must guarantee that there will be no similar incidents in the future. If the above points can be achieved, not only will the doubts of the Chinese people be completely dispelled, but it will also be enough to show your bank's candor. At the same time, the association will also declare its dissolution. Since your bank has been able to realize the past, there is no reason to refuse the future. Therefore, I hereby send this letter, hoping for a concrete reply."

Overseas Chinese Expelled from Japan 125

City Government Distributes Relief Funds

Eighth Group Arrives in Shanghai This Afternoon

According to the New News Agency, after arriving in Shanghai, the overseas Chinese expelled from Japan have been struggling to make ends meet in hotels due to unfamiliarity with the local area. They petitioned the city government for relief. The city government, finding their situation pitiable, invited representatives from the sixth group to negotiate at the central district yesterday morning. The overseas Chinese sent Wu Wentian and He Jinqian as representatives at 9:00 AM yesterday. They were received by Yuan, a clerk from the Second Division, who provided each person with a relief fund of five yuan, totaling thirty yuan for six people (note that the sixth group had ten people, four of whom have already returned to their hometowns). After receiving the money, the representatives returned to their lodgings and distributed it. According to the overseas Chinese representatives, they are deeply grateful to the mayor for providing five yuan per person. However, they have been in Shanghai for ten days, and the accumulated debt for room and board is already substantial. The money they received is insufficient to cover their debts, and they lack funds to return home. Today, representatives Zhu Wanglai and He Jinqian went to the Provincial Association to petition, but to no avail. They earnestly hope that the authorities will provide further relief to prevent them from wandering in a foreign land and starving to death. As for the ninth group of nine overseas Chinese, the Japanese ship Tsukuba Maru is scheduled to arrive at the port at 4:00 PM this afternoon. Those arriving in Shanghai this time are overseas Chinese detained by the Minamisenju Police Station in Tokyo.

The Chinese Navigation Officers' Association and the Chinese Maritime Navigation Officers' Mutual Aid Association are both organizations composed of senior crew members of domestic river and sea vessels. Case of China Industrial Bank 131

Ministry of Finance Consults City Government for Investigation and Reply

According to the New Sound News Agency, the liquidators of the China Industrial Bank, lawyer Zhang Ding and accountant Xu Chao, are not only handling the registration of creditors but also working with the head office to take over the account books of various branches to facilitate the liquidation. The Ministry of Finance attaches great importance to the bank and has consulted the Shanghai Municipal Government to investigate and report on the capital of the China Industrial Bank for verification. It is heard that the Municipal Government, after receiving the order, instructed the Social Affairs Bureau to comply. A reporter from the New Sound News Agency learned from banking circles yesterday that the China Industrial Bank was founded in January of the 14th year of the Republic (1925) and was approved for registration by the former Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce in March of the 16th year of the Republic (1927). Since the establishment of the National Government, all banks have been required to re-register with the National Government and the Ministry of Finance, but the bank has not yet complied.

Landlords Force Eviction 137

Residents of Wuzhen Road Shantytowns Petition for Prohibition

The Area Was Purely Water Decades Ago

Residents Labored to Fill the Foundation Before They Could Settle

According to the New Sound News Agency, the residents of the tin-skinned shantytowns in the open space between Wuzhen Road, Xinmin Road, and Xinjiang Road in Zhabei have repeatedly petitioned the authorities to stop landlords from forcing them to move. The residents of the district specially petitioned the municipal party headquarters yesterday, requesting a thorough investigation. The original text stated that the area was purely water during the Guangxu years of the Qing Dynasty. Later, it was filled by residents, and shantytowns were built sixteen years ago. At that time, Hengli Company claimed to be the owner of the property and ordered the shantytowns to pay rent ranging from one yuan to ten yuan per month. Eighteen years ago, Deshun Company came forward, prohibiting the construction of shantytowns along the road and increasing the rent to tens to hundreds of yuan per year. Twenty years ago, Decheng Company forced the residents to move, which involved a lawsuit in court. Because the landlord had no contract, it was resolved through mediation. Since then, shops and residents have signed leases, but the shantytown residents have not. Now, in the name of Yu Chang Company, they are being forced to move. They should consider the hardships of the shantytown residents who filled the foundation and restrict the forced eviction. It was decided at a meeting of the shantytown residents yesterday that they would petition the Social Affairs Bureau at 9:00 AM on the 15th to prohibit it.

Southeast Transportation Exhibition Concludes 138

Zhejiang Scenic Area Tourism Bureau Established

Ticket Sales and Other Matters Entrusted to China Travel Service

The Southeast Transportation Exhibition was postponed by order of Chairman Chiang. The exhibition preparatory committee completed its work at the end of September. The Zhejiang Scenic Area Tourism Bureau was officially established on October 1 to take over all matters of the Transportation Exhibition and conduct scenic area tourism work. The office is located in the Construction Department. The director and deputy director of the bureau are concurrently held by Director Zeng and Mayor Zhou, and Ye Jiajun, the chief of the First Section of the Construction Department, is appointed as concurrently as the general manager. The internal staff will be transferred from some of the former exhibition staff. The establishment of the bureau is modeled after the establishment of tourism bureaus in Europe and the United States, with the aim of revitalizing the rural economy. The organization of various scenic areas and the facilities of stations, telephones, and hotels along the lines have been prepared by the former Transportation Exhibition, which can be said to be largely completed. Therefore, the bureau can start selling tickets for tourism after a little arrangement. It has been agreed that the China Travel Service will handle ticket sales in Shanghai in the future, and business offices and information desks will be established in Shanghai, Hangzhou, Ningbo, Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway, and the Hangzhou City Main Bus Station to facilitate travel.

Disposal of Morphine Agency Confiscated Items 147

Raw Materials and Machines Are Confiscated

Cars Are Judged to Be in the Custody of the Court

Cai Bicheng, a Sichuanese who served as a county magistrate in Sichuan, came to Shanghai with his family after becoming rich through his official position, residing at No. 24 Qinyuan Village, Xinzha, and believing that the manufacture of morphine could yield double the profits, he leased a newly built four-story mansion at Nos. 175-177 Avenue Road from Dayao Construction Company on the Museum Road, established a factory, and recruited those skilled in this technique to refine it from opium. Unexpectedly, on the morning of the Double Tenth Festival, due to careless work, a fire suddenly broke out in the factory. Cai heard the news at home and immediately fled with his wife and important documents in a car. Most of the factory employees also fled, with only three people, including Long Baochang, being captured. The trial judge of the First Special District Local Court, Liu Yugui, and the bailiff's lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, went to the factory and Cai Bicheng's residence to inspect the factory on the afternoon of the day before yesterday. They deeply felt the greatness of the factory. Even compared with the morphine factory opened by the Japanese at No. 1 Huanglu Road in the past, it was still a small wizard seeing a big wizard. After the inspection was completed, Cai's family had already taken away anything of value when Cai fled, but there was still a lot of heavy furniture. The bailiff could not send personnel to guard it for a long time. After Judge Liu approved the bailiff to withdraw the guarding detectives, he immediately ordered Cai's mother-in-law, Gan Yang, to be responsible for the safekeeping. At that time, the lady stated that her son-in-law and daughter had fled this time, and she did not know when they would return, requesting that the safekeeping period be specified, otherwise the rent would not be paid when it was due, and the landlord would force them to move. Judge Liu felt that the lady's statement seemed true, so he ordered her to keep it until the end of this month, and then decide on it again when it was due. As for the four large and small machines, sixteen tanks full of morphine-soaked water, more than twenty coal stoves, and a large number of wooden boxes, glass bottles, bundles of dry and wet wool, etc. in the factory, which were either raw materials for manufacture or tools for manufacture, there were many pieces and heavy quantities, and it was impossible to move them. Since the fire was extinguished by the fire brigade, the Xinzha bailiff has been sending Chinese and foreign bailiffs to guard the area day and night in shifts to prevent theft. Yesterday morning, the bailiff, believing that the agency had been clarified by the judge's inspection and that it was not necessary to maintain the status quo for a long time, drew up a list of all the items and a car owned by Cai Bicheng that was found in the Qiu's car room on Xiejiao Road, and asked the bailiff's lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, to apply to Judge Liu for disposal in court to avoid continued guarding. Judge Liu ruled that all morphine raw materials and equipment for manufacturing morphine would be confiscated, and the wool, ethyl alcohol, etc. would be handed over to the bailiff for auction, and the proceeds would be sent to the court for safekeeping. As for the car that was intercepted, it should also be temporarily stored in the court for safekeeping.

Hankou Road Shops Again Request Cancellation of One-Way Traffic 148

If the Municipal Council Only Considers the Convenience of Car Owners,

Then the Rights of Shops Will Be Deprived and Obligations Will No Longer Be Fulfilled

The shops on Hankou Road, due to the significant impact on their business since the implementation of one-way traffic on that road, previously jointly sent a letter to the Municipal Council requesting its swift cancellation. Recently, it was reported on the fifth of this month that the Municipal Council not only did not accept the shops' request, but also considered changing the one-way traffic on that road to a full-day eastward or westward direction. The shops on Hankou Road believe that this measure would be fatal to their business, and therefore sent another letter to the Municipal Council a few days ago, stating:

"Regarding the fact that our businesses have suffered a drastic decline in sales since the implementation of one-way traffic on Hankou Road, we jointly sent a letter to your bureau on August 30th, requesting its abolition. Now, reading the report on the fifth of this month, your bureau not only does not accept our request, but even intensifies the situation by considering changing the one-way traffic to a full-day eastward or westward direction. If this proposal is implemented, it will inconvenience customers driving to purchase goods, as it was in the past. Furthermore, various vehicles that currently travel back and forth on Hankou Road four times a day will only travel twice, and those that travel back and forth twice a day will only travel once. With the reduced number of vehicle trips, the opportunity for shops to attract customers through storefront displays will also inevitably decrease. The overall business on the entire road will become even more unimaginable. Moreover, according to reports, the Director of Public Works stated at a Traffic Committee meeting that 'one-way traffic on Hankou Road is indeed more convenient for automobiles.' To prioritize the convenience of a small number of car-owning citizens, your bureau is willing to harm the business of all the shops on the road. We are all tax-paying citizens, yet the treatment we receive is so unfair. We wonder how your bureau will justify this. If you say that shops are closing down due to economic depression, consider the commercial situation on Hankou Road, which has always been known for its prosperity. Now, let's take the four parallel roads between Nanjing Road and Edward Road as an example. The number of closed and vacant shops is not as high as on Hankou Road. It is clear that one-way traffic has a significant impact on the entire road's business, and there is no room for forceful arguments. If your bureau insists on continuing to implement one-way traffic, or even takes a step further and implements the full-day eastward or westward direction, then the rights that our businesses should enjoy will be deprived, and our obligations will naturally be impossible to fulfill. We hereby make a solemn statement and request your investigation. This is addressed to the Public Concession Municipal Council, from Fuchang Gift Shop on Hankou Road and more than a hundred other businesses."

### Robbery on Hongqiao Road in the Middle of the Night 151

Guo Shouhong Bravely Fights Off Robbers

A Sewing Machine is Stolen

Fei Rongqu, from Anhui, lives in a small house at No. 1 Taoyuan Village, Hongqiao Road, Xujiahui, Shanghai. He works as an inspector at the Lin Sheng Military Uniform Manufacturing Factory, earning a monthly salary of twenty yuan. At around 5:00 AM yesterday morning, while Fei was fast asleep, he suddenly heard urgent knocking on the door. Fei got up to inquire, and the voice claimed to be from the Public Security Bureau investigating reactionary elements. Since Fei believed they were public officials, he had no doubts and immediately opened the door. However, the visitors were not police officers. Among the five people, one was wearing a worn-out Western suit, one was wearing a silk long gown, and the rest were wearing blue and black cloth short shirts and trousers. They spoke with a northern accent and held pistols and axes. Seeing the bad situation, Fei Rongqu immediately questioned them loudly. One of them immediately swung an ax at his head. Fortunately, Fei dodged quickly and was not hit. During the struggle, Fei's brother-in-law, Guo Shouhong, came out to see what was happening. Seeing the emergency, he bravely stepped forward, grabbed the assailant around the waist, and snatched the ax. Seeing that they could not succeed, the assailants howled and fled, stealing a sewing machine before leaving. Fei and others hurriedly chased after them, but were scared back by the thugs firing two shots into the air. They then turned to the Xujiahui Branch Bureau in charge of the area to report and request pursuit.

### Beating Mother Sentineced to Six Months in Prison 152

Shu Zhixi, a Qingpu native residing at No. 5 Dingchang Alley, Lagenac Road, French Concession, is 25 years old this year. He used to work at Yunfei Motor Company, but has been unemployed and idle since it closed. He is fond of alcohol and cannot live without it at every meal. At noon on the 3rd of this month, Shu asked his mother, Ni (65 years old this year), for money to buy alcohol. Not getting what he wanted, he became unhappy and argued with his mother, eventually throwing a wine pot and injuring his mother's right cheek, causing swelling. His mother reported this to the French Police, who sent detectives to arrest Shu and send him to the Special No. 2 Court. The police lawyer filed a public prosecution for the crime of injuring a close relative. The details have been reported in previous newspapers. The trial was concluded by Judge Li Changnian, and yesterday morning, Judge Li presented the case in the Criminal Division One court, sentencing Shu Zhixi to six months of imprisonment for injuring his direct line mother. The number of days detained before the judgment is confirmed will be deducted from the imprisonment period at a rate of two days for one day of imprisonment. During the appeal period, the defendant will be transferred to the detention center.

### In the Five-Life Burning Ship Case 153

Victims Request the Arrest of the Arsonist Chen Yunqing

On the night of September 10th at 12:00 AM, a fire broke out at the Chen Rongfa Sofa Shop at No. 1350 Zhonghua Road, Nanshi, resulting in the tragic death of five people, including adults and children. The news vendor Cheng Yonglin, who lived in a small room, holding his eight-year-old son Ruiqing, rushed out through the smoke. The boy was burned to death, and Cheng himself suffered severe burns. Due to the pain of losing his son and the shock, he was overstimulated and has been receiving treatment at Qu Zhifu Hospital ever since, still not out of danger. Furthermore, he is poor and cannot afford medical expenses. Chen Yunqing, the owner of the Chen Rongfa Sofa Shop where the fire started, lived on the front floor and escaped unharmed by climbing down a rope. He had insured against fire with British and American insurance companies for one thousand taels and has been hiding in the concession. The Municipal Police Bureau has repeatedly tried to arrest him without success. Now, Cheng's wife, Zhou, has learned that Chen Yunqing has arranged for someone to obtain one thousand yuan in insurance compensation, allowing him to live freely in the concession, disregarding the lives of others. She has filed a complaint with the Local Court and Public Security Bureau, accusing him of arson for compensation and causing the death of five people, requesting that Chen Yunqing be arrested and punished severely. A few days ago, the Wenmiao Police Station managed to arrest the arsonist Chen Yunqing, interrogated him briefly, and transferred him to the General Bureau for strict legal action.

Recently, due to the mutiny in the county, County Chief Tang resigned, and the county administration was without a leader, causing panic among the people. The association immediately telegraphed the central, southwestern, and other agencies, asking them to select capable personnel to succeed him. The original telegram is copied below:

"To the National Government of Nanjing, the Executive Yuan, and the Ministry of Interior, and to the West and Southwest Political Affairs Committee of Guangzhou, the Provincial Government, the Department of Civil Affairs, and the Central District Pacification Commissioner's Office:

Upon receiving the telegrams, we are alarmed to learn that an incident has occurred in our county and that County Chief Tang has resigned suddenly, leaving the county administration without a leader, causing panic among the people. Our association members are deeply concerned about our homeland and are extremely anxious. We believe that the county administration cannot remain vacant, and the successor should be selected by your government. We respectfully suggest that Mr. Xiao Hanzong, Mr. Zhu Zhuowen, and Mr. Chen Qingyun from our county are either pioneers of the Party or revolutionary youth, well-educated and talented, and capable of being competent. They all come from rural backgrounds and understand the hardships of the people. They have all served their homeland in the past and have gained a good reputation. To make them the forerunners of model county administration would satisfy the people's expectations. Therefore, we contribute our knowledge and respectfully request your government to consider the situation, and quickly select one of Xiao Hanzong, Zhu Zhuowen, or Chen Qingyun to succeed the county chief of Zhongshan County, to calm the people's hearts and relieve their suffering, and to demonstrate the model county administration. We would be extremely grateful and await your orders.

Zhongshan Model County Administration Facility Promotion Association Shanghai General Association Yuan Yin."

The inspection report on the issuance reserve of the China Land Reclamation Bank states that the issuance reserve and operating reserve of the China Land Reclamation Bank have always been completely separated. On the 13th of this month, accountant Wang Zikang, together with board representatives Xu Jiqing and Xu Busun, conducted an inspection, and the results are as follows:

Total amount of exchange coupons issued: 6,868,000 silver dollars

Total amount of exchange coupon reserve: 6,868,000 silver dollars

Including:

Cash reserve: 5,056,000 silver dollars

Guarantee reserve: 1,812,000 silver dollars

The above two items indicate that the cash reserve is above 70% and the guarantee reserve is below 30%. This is a special report. 723, 10, 13
