Second Branch of the High Court Approves Bail for Pan Hongsheng for Medical Treatment 161

Pan's Mother's Plea for Release, Every Word a Tear

Patriotic heroes Pan Hongsheng and Liu Chongwu, and others, organized a national salvation assassination group, throwing bombs as a warning to treacherous merchants, and were arrested and sentenced to twelve years in prison by the court. Later, all sectors held a meeting to rescue them, and hired lawyer Ma Junshuo and others to file an appeal. After trial by the Second Branch of the High Court, the sentence was reduced to six years. They were immediately sent to prison for execution. Recently, Pan has been suffering from severe hemoptysis. His mother, Shi, was extremely anxious upon hearing the news at home, and complained to the Patriotic Heroes Support Association, asking the original defense lawyer Ma to submit a petition to the court, requesting that the court consider the tragic situation and grant bail for medical treatment. The wording was quite tragic and tactful. The court has now notified that bail for medical treatment has been approved. Their petition and the notification are recorded separately below:

Pan Shi's Petition

"For the sake of a lung disease that is becoming increasingly dangerous, with life hanging by a thread, requesting consideration of the tragic situation, and approval of bail for medical treatment.

My son, Hongsheng, and Liu Chongwu, and others, because of their enthusiasm for patriotism and outrage at injustice, warned merchants who were selling Japanese goods. They asked themselves whether they had premeditated murder or selfish intentions. The police prosecuted them for suspected murder, and after repeated trials, the Supreme Court sent it back for retrial. The Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, considering that they were burdened due to public affairs and that the crime was forgivable, reduced the sentence to six years. My son, in admiration of your kindness, and because various groups in this city petitioned the government for a special pardon, the Judicial Yuan instructed the Second Branch of the High Court to submit the case file after the case was confirmed, so that it could be reviewed. Therefore, my son decided to waive the right to appeal. The case was confirmed. However, my son's physical condition was weak. Since being detained, the physical and mental suffering he has endured cannot be fully described. As a result, he contracted pulmonary tuberculosis, and often coughs up blood, even filling a basin. When the retrial was held, his face was pale and he could not stand. Although he had repeatedly requested bail for medical treatment, the prison officials did not pay attention to his actual condition, and there was no sufficient medical proof. He was not approved. Later, the prison officials moved my son to the prison hospital (in Tilanqiao Prison), but because he was in a state of unfreedom and in an extraordinary environment, he could not get adequate treatment. Therefore, his lung disease worsened day by day, with no improvement. He could not eat and could not sleep at night. He could not stand for a moment, and he was exhausted after speaking a few words. Now, due to excessive coughing up blood, plus a dry cough, his face is pale and black. His life is in danger, and his death is imminent. My daughter, Huizhu, often visits the prison and knows the details best. Recently, the original defense lawyer, Ma Junshuo, reported to the prison officials, who also found that my son's condition was critical and had already moved him to the fifth floor of the hospital (the severity of the illness is directly proportional to the number of floors). They also agreed to be responsible for providing evidence when the court investigates, in order to facilitate bail for medical treatment. Based on this, my son's life is in danger, which is a most obvious fact. Moreover, my husband and I are both over sixty years old, old and frail. Our clothing and food depend on Hongsheng's labor. My husband is sick and blind, and I am also depressed and in pain. If Hongsheng dies in prison, my husband and I will surely die together. Being sentenced to imprisonment is equivalent to a death sentence, and it will inevitably affect the lives of the entire family. The tragedy of life is extreme. I respectfully ask your court to consider the circumstances of the crime and to grant temporary release for medical treatment in order to maintain life and show compassion. This is both in the public interest. Respectfully, Shanghai First Special District Court,"

High Branch Notification 162

Jiangsu High Court Second Branch Notification,

"According to the applicant, her son Pan Hongsheng's lung disease is becoming increasingly dangerous, his life is hanging by a thread, and she requests bail for medical treatment. This court has sent a letter to the Municipal Council, asking them to order the prison to investigate and reply. The Municipal Council Prison has replied and attached a medical certificate to the court. After investigation, the prisoner is suffering from tuberculosis, and the prison doctor has certified that he should be granted bail for medical treatment. In addition to notifying the prison to investigate, we hereby notify the applicant to apply to the Municipal Council Prison for bail for medical treatment. This notification is addressed to the applicant Pan Shi."

We will promote your virtues. We respectfully beseech you to agree, and we will be extremely grateful."

The Outcome of University Student Huang Naiwu Injuring a Dancer 167

Compensation of Three Thousand Yuan, Private Lawsuit Resolved

The Criminal Part is Still Under Appeal

Huang Naiwu, a university student from Jiangxi, harbored a grudge against Li Xiuying, a Tianjin dancer at the Da Hu Dance Hall. At around 10:00 PM on June 20th of this year, Huang invited the rascal Jiang Ada from Suzhou to bring nitrate corrosive liquid to the Da Hu Dance Hall, intending to pour it on Li's face to disfigure her and vent his anger. Unexpectedly, Jiang accidentally poured it on another dancer, Qiu Lifei, causing injuries to her face and body. The police arrested Huang and Jiang and prosecuted them in the Special No. 2 Court for the crime of injury. Huang and Jiang were each sentenced to eight months in prison. Huang disagreed and appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court, which changed the sentence to three years in prison. The victim Qiu Lifei hired lawyer Wu Peng to file a supplementary private lawsuit, seeking damages of 48,000 yuan. The first instance judgment was transferred to the Civil Division, where Judge Wu Xiaoke summoned the parties twice. The details have been reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday, there was a continued hearing. The plaintiff arrived with lawyer Wu, and the defendants Huang Naiwu and Jiang Ada also separately submitted proposals from the detention center and prison. Judge Wu questioned the parties in the Seventh Tribunal and immediately advised them to reconcile, ordering the plaintiff to make concessions and instructing Huang Naiwu to increase the amount. Huang started with several hundred yuan, and finally Huang agreed to pay 3,000 yuan, which must be paid by the end of the year. With the consent of the plaintiff Qiu Lifei, a reconciliation was reached in court. The two parties signed a reconciliation record and withdrew. Huang was sent back to the detention center to await the judgment of the third instance appeal, and Jiang was sent back to the Special No. 2 Prison by the police to serve his sentence.

###芝巴德 Ship's Crew Bravely Rescues

瑞華 Ship's Crew

瑞華 ship caught fire, 28 crew members sent to Xiamen

The 芝巴德 ship, which travels to the South Seas Islands, went from Shanghai to Xiamen this time. In the waters of Fuzhou, it encountered a Chinese merchant ship that caught fire and was completely burned down and sunk. Twenty-eight crew members and sailors were fortunately rescued by the Dutch ship at the risk of their lives. Yesterday, Java Company received a detailed report from the owner of the 芝巴德 ship. The details are as follows:

###瑞華 Caught Fire

The Dutch ship荷巴德 was on its way from Shanghai to Java. On the 1st of this month, in the waters between Fuzhou and Xiamen, it encountered strong winds and huge waves. The 芝巴德 ship, while moving forward, saw a Chinese merchant ship named 瑞華 in the waters there, which was already on fire. The flames were quite intense, and the fire was already coming out of the deck. The ship had already sent out a distress signal, but no other ship was going to rescue it. At that time, the wind and waves were huge, and the people on board had no hope of escaping except to wait for death.

Dutch Ship to the Rescue In this hurricane and giant waves, the owner of the 芝巴德 ship, seeing this ship on fire and sending out a distress signal, did not hesitate to overcome difficulties and decided to risk great danger to sail to the rescue. At that time, the太古 Company's 济南 ship also passed by the area. After the Dutch ship requested assistance, they bravely went to rescue. However, the wind and waves were too strong, and the 芝巴德 ship could not get close. Therefore, they asked the 济南 ship to get close and stop, taking on the responsibility of blocking the wind. Then, the Dutch ship risked approaching and carried out rescue work.

Valiant and Commendable The owner of the 芝巴德 ship immediately gathered all the crew members and asked who dared to take this great risk, go into the burning ship to rescue people. At that time, all the crew members said they were willing to go, but the owner did not allow it, saying that this adventure was not ordinary and could not guarantee that they would not sacrifice their own lives. At that time, it was decided to choose young crew members who did not have wives and children, put the sampan into the sea, and advance through the terrifying winds and waves. After encountering nine deaths and one life, they finally reached the burning ship and rescued the crew members who were waiting for death.

Entire Crew Rescued A total of twenty-eight crew members and sailors were rescued from the 瑞華 ship at the risk of their lives. The people on board were all rescued. Fortunately, the assistance of the济南 ship helped the twenty-eight people to survive. They were immediately taken to the 芝巴德 ship. The crew members who went to rescue had endured all kinds of hardships. Now, all the crew members of 瑞華 have been sent to Xiamen to go ashore. The 瑞華 ship that caught fire sank into the sea a few minutes after the crew members were rescued. The cargo was completely lost. The owner of the 芝巴德 ship has telegraphed the detailed situation to the Shanghai company.

A Gangster Using the Name of the Communist Party to Extort Money 168

Demanding 5,000 Yuan from Gu Changfa, a Shipyard Owner

After Sending Four Letters and Changing Hotels Three Times, He Was Finally Arrested

Gu Changfa, a local resident, started his shipyard business in Gaomu Bridge East, Lujiazui, Pudong, making him a relatively well-off family. A gangster coveted his wealth. On the 19th of last month, Gu received a letter signed by Lu Jieqiu, "Minister of the Administrative Department of the Chinese Communist Party." The letter claimed the department was short of funds and had heard that Gu was quite generous, requesting his righteous assistance with a temporary loan of 5,000 yuan. If he agreed, he should place a square piece of red paper on a utility pole near the tofu shop east of Gu's residence on the main street within three days to indicate his acceptance. It instructed him to wrap the full amount in cash with paper and then with a piece of clothing, and then wrap that in newspaper. The surface should state it was to be delivered to Lu Jieqiu. He was to wait in a room at the Asia Hotel in the French Concession. On the 3rd of this month, he received a fourth letter instructing Gu to deliver the money as agreed. Detailed Account of a Dutch Ship's Accident 172

The Cargo in the Middle Hold Was Completely Destroyed

Consisting Entirely of Goods Imported into Shanghai

The Dutch East Asia Company's cargo ship "Zuidkerk," managed by the Java Shipping Company in Shanghai, experienced an accident en route from Europe to Shanghai, resulting in significant damage to the cargo destined for Shanghai. The situation is currently under investigation. The following is a report from yesterday.

Fire in the Middle Hold: The "Zuidkerk," a regular cargo ship of the Dutch Company's Europe-China route, with a displacement of 10,000 tons, was carrying a large quantity of goods from Rotterdam and Amsterdam in the Netherlands to Shanghai. Originally scheduled to arrive in Shanghai on November 8th, at 8:00 AM on November 8th, a fire broke out in the middle hold of the ship while it was in the Suez Canal. The fire spread rapidly, engulfing all sides of the middle hold. The steel plates of the ship's hull were burned red and warped. The fire also spread to the engine room, damaging the machinery.

Telegram for Rescue: The Shanghai Java Company did not receive a detailed telegram from the shipowner until the 12th, stating that after the fire broke out, the entire crew worked to extinguish the fire, using five pumps to spray water. However, because the fire was in the middle hold, the water could not reach it. The shipowner then devised a plan to cut five large holes in the thick steel plates of the middle hold to allow water to enter. At that time, the shipowner sent out a distress signal. Fire boats in the canal and nearby merchant ships also came to help. After three days and nights of fire, the fire inside the ship was extinguished, but the damage was significant.

Cargo Loss: The cargo onboard was mostly imported to Shanghai, with the largest portion in the middle hold consisting of a large quantity of paper and cardboard. In addition, there was fake fertilizer, mostly ordered by local Chinese merchants, which was completely burned. The cargo in other holds was fortunate to be isolated, resulting in less damage. A large quantity of gunpowder in the dangerous hold (destined for Japan) was fortunately soaked in water, avoiding an explosion. The destroyed cargo has been inspected by an appraiser, and the amount of damage will be telegraphed after verification. Transshipment of Cargo: Yesterday, the company received a second telegram stating that the cargo was being unloaded at that location. Seven hundred tons of cargo and 350 tons of coal have been landed, and the rest is still being unloaded. It has been decided that the undamaged cargo destined for various ports in the East will be transshipped to Shanghai because the hull of the "Zuidkerk" requires extensive repairs and cannot sail at this time. The company has already notified the local cargo owners yesterday.

Car Accident Kills Female College Student 173

Trial Begins in Case Involving Student

Deceased's Mother Demands 99,000 Yuan in Compensation

Judge Instructs Private Suit Portion to Be Resolved Out of Court

On September 20th of this year, around 10:00 AM, female students Wu Yongmei, Hua Shuxian, Ouyang Shu, and Luo Qiaoyun from Jinan University in Zhenru went out to wash photos at the Yuyuan Photo Studio on the south side of the railway station. Unexpectedly, near the Jiaotong Road, about twenty steps from the school gate, a car with license plate number 3021 suddenly drove up from behind and struck three of the four female students (Luo Qiaoyun was spared). All were sent to the hospital for treatment. Wu Yongmei died upon arrival because her skull was crushed. Hua Shuxian and Ouyang Shu were hospitalized for treatment. The driver, Lan Fuming, was detained by the Third Precinct of the Fourth District and sent to the local court for questioning. Details were reported in previous newspapers. It is now known that this case has been thoroughly investigated by Prosecutor Zhang Zi, who ordered that Lan Fuming be released on bail of 1,600 yuan, guaranteed in writing by a shop. At the same time, Lan Fuming was prosecuted in criminal court for

Causing Death by Negligence 174

Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, Judge Zhang Shao specially convened the Fifth Court for trial. The plaintiff, the deceased's mother Wu Kongshi, hired lawyer Su Fonan as her private lawsuit representative. The defendant, Lan Fuming, hired lawyers Wang Zaoshi and Lan Ren to defend him. Lan Fuming stated that he was 22 years old, from Guangdong, and resided at 87 Yan Hai Road, Lao Beimen. On September 20th, he was driving a car from Zhenru back to Shanghai when he accidentally caused the accident near Jinan University. The judge asked why he didn't stop the car when there were people in front of him. He replied that he did not intentionally cause the accident. The judge said that if it were intentional, he would be charged with murder. The prosecutor is now prosecuting him for causing death by negligence. If he had stopped at the time, the,

Tragic accident would not have happened. Lan replied that there was nothing he could do. Hua Shuxian testified that she was 22 years old, from Jiangxi, and a student at Jinan University. On that day, she and Wu Yongmei and the other two were going out to wash photos. She and Wu Yongmei were walking shoulder to shoulder, she on the left. She was knocked to the ground and fainted, and did not remember hearing the car's horn. Ouyang Shu testified that she was 20 years old, from Jiangxi. The four of them were walking in pairs, both on the left side of the road. She was behind, walking forward along the wooden posts, but the car should not have been driving fast near the school entrance, nor should it have failed to honk the horn. She was also knocked to the ground, and because there were wooden posts next to her, even if she wanted to avoid it, she could not. The judge ordered a diagram to be drawn in court and kept on file. The judge called Luo Qiaoyun to the stand, who testified that she was 21 years old, from Jiangxi, and a student at Jinan University, and corroborated the above statements. She also said that Wu Yongmei and Hua Shuxian were in front, and she

And Ouyang Shu were in the back, walking in two rows, about ten steps from the school, walking along the wooden posts. Unexpectedly, the car that caused the accident did not honk its horn and drove forward quickly. Ouyang Shu was immediately knocked to the ground. Because she was walking on the left side, she saw it and avoided it by going onto the sand pile on the side of the road, escaping danger. If the car had stopped at that time, Wu Yongmei would not have died tragically. Instead, it crashed straight forward, knocking down both Wu Yongmei and Hua Shuxian who were walking in front, crushing Wu Yongmei, and causing the tragedy because of the brain injury. Furthermore, the road was very wide, etc. Finally, Zhang Liancheng testified that he was a police officer in the Third Precinct of the Fourth District, stationed near Jinan University. About ten steps from his post, there were four female students walking in front and back. At that time, his (referring to the defendant's) car was driving very fast. He saw it and directed him, but he

Still Drove Fast 175

Whether he was doing it on purpose or not listening to his command, he did not know. The judge asked if he was driving the car. He answered yes, but there was a woman sitting next to him. At this point, the judge asked Hua Shuxian and Ouyang Shu how much they were seeking in private compensation. They replied that they were seeking a total of 400 yuan in medical expenses and 3,000 yuan each in mental distress damages, for a total of 6,400 yuan. The plaintiff's private lawsuit lawyer stated that the private lawsuit plaintiff, Wu Kong Yude, was the mother of Wu Yongmei. Wu Yongmei was a third-year student at Jinan University in Zhenru, and she was recognized by the school authorities for her excellent character and academics. Yongmei was young and orphaned, and was the oldest in the family. The family was poor. After graduating from university, they were counting on her to support her parents and raise her younger siblings. Unexpectedly, this time, the defendant Lan Fuming drove his own car

Crashing Recklessly 176

Causing Wu Yongmei to be struck and killed. Now the defendant is treating the car as a toy and human life as grass. In the criminal aspect, he should be punished. In the civil aspect, he should be strictly ordered to pay compensation. Wu Yongmei was only 23 years old. After graduating from university, she could have served society for at least 35 years. At an average of 200 yuan per month, that is 2,400 yuan per year. For 35 years, she would have earned 84,000 yuan. The educational expenses spent on Yongmei for 23 years totaled 10,000 yuan. The cost of transporting the coffin back to Jiangxi and the funeral expenses totaled 5,000 yuan. The total requested compensation is 99,000 yuan, etc. The judge ordered the defendant Lan Fuming to the stand and asked, "Now that the private lawsuit is seeking 99,000 yuan plus 6,400 yuan, how do you plan to handle it?" Lan replied, "Where would I get such a large sum? Two or three thousand yuan might be possible to raise." The judge then instructed both lawyers to resolve the private lawsuit portion out of court. The public lawsuit portion requires further investigation and will be scheduled for another joint trial. The defendant Lan Fuming was released on 5,000 yuan bail, guaranteed by a reliable shop, pending further instructions.

Police in Dachang Beat Villager to Death 177

Public Outrage Among Villagers Leads to Protest at Police Station

Autopsy Completed Yesterday, Police Chief Detained Pending Investigation

At 2:00 PM the day before yesterday, Wu Zhen, the director of the Dachang Police Station of the Baoshan County Public Security Bureau, sent police chief Song Wentong, police officer Chen Zhongshu, and five others to catch gamblers in Miaoxiang Village and Hujiazhuang, more than five miles northeast of the town. The police encountered brothers Zhang Jianrong and Zhang Jiansheng, villagers (i.e., local security guards) from Yemaodun, pushing a small cart of cotton to sell in order to pay their grain tax in Dachang, as the deadline was approaching. Therefore, they were pushing the cart very fast. The police, suspecting that Zhang and others were rushing to report the gambling bust, ordered them to stop. Zhang and others replied that the grain tax would increase tomorrow if they did not pay it. At first, they had a slight verbal altercation, which then escalated into a physical altercation. The police were all wearing plain clothes, with their uniforms underneath, so the villagers, Zhang Jianrong, etc., did not initially know they were police officers. A fight ensued, with the officers using their pistols and handguns to beat them. Zhang and others were beaten and fell to the ground. The police chief and others, realizing they had caused trouble, fled. The villagers from the surrounding villages, hearing that the police had beaten and injured the village security guards, rushed over and carried the most severely injured Zhang Jianrong to the Dachang Police Station. About a thousand men, women, and children protested at the entrance of the police station, creating a chaotic scene. Fortunately, a local gentleman from the town intervened to mediate, and the injured man was carried back for treatment. However, his injuries were too severe, and he soon died. Yesterday, the county magistrate sent Investigator Li Shou Xuan and more than twenty armed police officers to Dachang, where the autopsy revealed that the deceased, Zhang Jianrong, had bruises on both sides of his waist and his right eye was also struck. The perpetrators, Police Chief Song Tongwen, Chen Zhongshu, etc., were taken to the county for investigation. During the autopsy, the deceased's mother, Yang (67 years old), wife, Xu (33 years old), brother-in-law, Liu Hongyuan, etc., led the deceased's thirteen-year-old son, Lin Xing, and ten-year-old daughter, Wu Mei, etc., demanding compensation. Investigator Li ordered a further investigation. The deceased was 33 years old. At the time of the beating, he also lost 16.4 yuan in cash.

Special Article: National Self-Reliance and Revival's Awareness (Continued) 188

Draft by Zhang Yuanruo

丨At the Chinese Vocational Education Society丨

3. How to Develop National Power: Where Does the "Power" Lie? Speaking of this, everyone must be eager to ask, how exactly should national power be developed? At the same time, where exactly does the "power" lie? Speaking of developing national power, people already paid attention to it and worked hard during the reform of the Qing Dynasty. Their idea was to have strong armor and sharp weapons, and to build guns, cannons, and warships. At that time, they thought that China was extraordinary. Foreigners brought warships to China to fight us. They were threatened by gunboat diplomacy and thought that they must also use machine guns and cannons to fight back. Therefore, the method of saving the country at that time was to have strong armor and sharp weapons, which they thought was the supreme way to develop national power. However, what was the result? The result was a disastrous defeat. During the First Sino-Japanese War, China's navy was even more substantial than Japan's, but why did it still fail? This proves that the previous method of developing national power was to abandon the fundamentals and pursue the superficial. "National power" cannot be developed solely from the surface. The result of such development is only superficial strength. It must be cultivated from the root to have practical results. Otherwise, even if we have airplanes, cannons, and foreign guns, our Chinese soldiers will still not know how to use them. Many people are superstitious and think that bullets have eyes, and whoever is destined to die will be shot to death. Also, I often hear soldiers say, "I am a martial artist and I have no knowledge." This is really a big mistake. To be a soldier, he needs a lot of knowledge. Taking cannon firing as an example, to fire accurately, he must have extremely profound mathematical knowledge to be able to hit the target every time. In ancient times, Chinese military strategists still needed various advanced knowledge, like Zhuge Liang, who was a famous Chinese military strategist. He could predict the future, and he could win by surprise. His so-called "borrowing the east wind" is generally thought to be mysterious, but in fact it is only because his knowledge was profound, so he could apply it freely. It has been the same since ancient times, and it is even more so today. Therefore, a military strategist today needs more knowledge, and he must not say that a soldier can do without knowledge. If he has no knowledge, then he is the same as a bandit. At the same time, if we only pay attention to strong armor and sharp weapons, and do not know how to cultivate "national power" from the root and from all aspects, then that is a way of abandoning the fundamentals and pursuing the superficial.

"National power," if we analyze it, includes many aspects: political, economic, military, social, educational, cultural, and everything else are components of national power. Not long ago, Dagong Daily published an essay entitled "The Basic Problems of National Defense," written by Mr. Ding Wenjiang. He said that China's national defense is extremely dangerous. If a war breaks out with a foreign country, China will be full of loopholes. When the chairman introduced me just now, he complimented me on how patriotic I am and how enthusiastic I am about promoting national goods, which is actually unnecessary. We must know that we Chinese are really pitiful. It is certainly very easy to buy foreign goods in peacetime, but once a war breaks out, even if we want to buy foreign goods, there is no place to buy them. If we don't have enough to wear and use, we can do without buying them, but even the rice we eat is not enough. Our industry is so undeveloped, and as a country that claims to be based on agriculture, we have to rely on others for food. If they block your coast, you will immediately become a fish in a bucket, with no way to survive. Speaking of transportation, it is really extremely pitiful. It only takes Russia a week to get to Dihua, while it takes us three months to go from Suiyuan to Xinjiang by camel and 20 days by car. Ladies and gentlemen, please go there. Do you have the courage to go? This is not to say that the Chinese have no ambition, but because of the inconvenience of transportation. It is not easy to go to Yunnan and Guizhou either. If we want to go there, we must take a foreign ship. Once I went to Europe and met many Chinese people on the ship. I asked him, "Are you also going to a foreign country?" He said, "I am going to Yunnan." Because of the inconvenience of transportation, they have to take such a detour. But if the French want to go, they can get there in a day or two. From this, we can see how dangerous our national defense is. Once the border is in emergency, enemy troops will arrive in the morning and reach the evening, but we are too far away to help. Therefore, speaking of China's national defense, the problem is not simple. We must start from many aspects, and at the same time, economic, social, and various undertakings must be developed to make national defense practical. In other words, we must first have national power before we can have national defense. However, how exactly do we develop our national power, and who will develop it? The reason why I advocate "self-reliance" is that it is the most practical way to strengthen national power. Self-reliance is the engine of strengthening national power, because to talk about self-reliance, we must first set an example. At least I must work hard to talk about self-reliance. Today, I encourage everyone, if we want to develop national power, we must start with each of us. As long as I bury my head and work hard, the result of hard work, little by little, bit by bit, is national power. National power comes from the hard work of the people. We don't have to look for national power elsewhere. Now, many people give up on themselves and think that the Chinese are really doomed to die, and that the Chinese are the most unpromising in the world. Therefore, everyone is unwilling to work hard. This is really suicide. We must be aware and correct this suicide, and believe that as long as we work hard, we will have national power. If we want to develop national power, we must promote self-reliance. "National power is contained in everyone, in my brain, in my hands. The power of each person is a component of national power. The sum of the separate and joint efforts of 400 million people is equal to the power of the nation. After the power of the nation is there, the country will naturally be strong, there is no problem. Is there any country in the world that has more great people than we Chinese, and is there any country with more people than us? There are 400 million and one people. The country is the accumulation of people. In the principles of political science, people are the essential element of the country. So as long as we all work hard, the result of hard work added together, this power is truly unparalleled. It can break the world record, overcome any national disaster, and defeat any powerful enemy. As long as the six families adhere to this principle, the result will be to develop national power.

[P Sports News: The Eleventh World Games

I am preparing to participate in six events

Soccer, Track and Field, Weightlifting, Swimming, Race Walking, Western Boxing

34 to 40 Athletes, 6 Staff Members

Selection Methods Generally Determined

Summer Camp to be Held in Qingdao Next Year

(Tianjin, 13th) The Planning Committee for Participation in the World Games held its first meeting at the National Hotel at 8 o'clock today. Attendees included Shen Sishi, Ma Yuehan, and Yuan Dunli. The following was resolved: (1) Prepare to participate in six events, including soccer, track and field, race walking, weightlifting, swimming, and Western boxing. (2) Various performance events, such as martial arts, must be approved by the World Games Committee and have sufficient funding. (3) The planned number of participants for each event: soccer 18, track and field 4 to 6, race walking 4, weightlifting, swimming, and Western boxing 2 to 4 each, for a total of 34 to 40 people. 6 to lower number for performance events. (4) Staff: Government representatives will be sent by the National Government, one representative from the Sports Association, two instructors, and two managers. (5) Athlete selection methods: (1) Preliminary selection will be made during the National Games. (2) For those with special excellent results, the standards will be set separately. (3) Sports experts will pay attention to the training of excellent talents at any time and report to the Sports Association. (4) Select excellent talents from the summer camp for continued training. (5) Selection by the Selection Committee organized by the Association. (6) Training methods: A summer camp will be held in Qingdao during the summer vacation of the 24th year to implement various sports training. Anyone who is willing to receive training can participate, and the methods will be determined separately. (7) Funding: 1. Request government subsidies, 2. The Association raises funds from all parties. (8) Ma Yuehan, Xu Minhui, Rong Qiguang, Song Junfu, Song Ruhai, Wu Yunrui, and Gao Xiwei are designated to be responsible for liaison and drum. (9) The Board of Directors shall designate one Chief Executive Officer to handle all matters related to preparing for and participating in the World Games. (10) The Board of Directors shall designate three committee members to formulate a summer camp plan. (11) In order to provide opportunities for those in the sports field to further their studies, those who wish to participate in the World Games may travel with the delegation. Those who meet the qualifications after review by the Association may be subsidized with sufficient funding, and the methods will be determined separately.

All-Around Sports 190

Liaoning Wins 1600m Relay (Tianjin, 13th) In the men's high 1600-meter relay, the participants were Ping, Ji, Liao, and Lu. Among the four teams, Liao and Ping had the strongest strength. Ping used Luo Qinglong and Zhang Guangshi to run the first and fourth legs, respectively. Liao used Wu Jingyao and Li Shiming to run the first and fourth legs, respectively. When the first leg was handed over, Wu was about one meter ahead of Luo. There was not much change in the second leg. In the third leg, Ping was five meters behind. Ji tried hard to catch up and was almost one meter behind Ping. In the fourth leg, Ping's Zhang Guangshi tried to catch up with Liao's Li Shiming. At 200 meters from the finish line, Li opened up his speed and finished the race about ten meters ahead of Zhang. As a result, Liao won with a time of 3 minutes 45.4 seconds, Ping second with a time of 3 minutes 48.4 seconds, Ji third, and Lu fourth.

Zhang Lingjia Collapses from Exhaustion 191

At 5 pm today, during the 400-meter race in the first half of the ten-event competition, Zhang Lingjia and Liao's Zhou Changxing competed fiercely. Zhang was in front for the first 200 meters. At 300 meters, Zhou overtook him. 50 meters from the finish line, Zhang desperately accelerated and overtook Zhou again. He reached the finish line, but collapsed due to excessive exertion. The health department of the conference injected him with a shot, but he has not yet recovered his spirit. He was admitted to the Municipal Hospital for recuperation in the evening. He may suspend participation in the second half of the ten-event competition on the 14th. (Another telegram) Zhang Lingjia has regained his spirit after being injected in the hospital. He was discharged from the hospital at night and will continue to participate in the second half of the ten-event competition on the 14th.

Volleyball Championship 192

Beiping Wins Junior High Title

Beiping Wins Junior High Championship (Tianjin, 13th) In the boys' junior high volleyball final, Henan faced Beiping. The first set was 22-20, the second set was 21-10, and the third set was 21-18. The overall result was 3-0, with Beiping winning and claiming the boys' junior high volleyball championship. This event took place at 8:30 AM, and it was raining at the time. The team members, due to the championship stakes, gave their all. In the first set, the scores from both sides increased alternately, with neither side yielding. Henan's front row blocking, spiking, and serving were powerful, while Beiping's ball-saving skills were unique. The game became even more intense when the score reached 20-20. Beiping then had the opportunity to serve, scoring two points and winning the set. In the second set, Beiping targeted Henan's back line with long-distance spikes, leaving Henan in a difficult position. In the third set, Henan tried hard to recover the losing situation. The second and third rows coordinated, using light passes to send the ball to the net, where the first row forcefully spiked it towards the Beiping team. This battle was extremely fierce, with scores increasing alternately until the score reached 18-17. Beiping again had the opportunity to serve, scoring several more points and ultimately winning the set. The Beiping team won the boys' junior high volleyball championship.

Senior High Beiping-Hebei Final (Tianjin, 13th) In the men's senior high volleyball semi-finals: (1) Beiping faced Shandong. Beiping won, securing the right to the final. The scores were 21-13 in the first set, with Beiping winning; 18-21 in the second set, with Beiping winning; 21-17 in the third set, with Shandong winning; and 21-11 in the fourth set, with Beiping winning. The overall result was 3-1. The competition between the two teams was particularly intense. The Beiping team excelled at saving balls. The back row's defensive techniques were refined, and they would dive to save the ball whenever there was danger. The front row's blocking and spiking were also very powerful. In the first set, after the score reached 12-14, they won effortlessly. In the second set, they targeted Shandong's back row with long-distance shots, achieving significant results. In the third set, Shandong tried its best to recover the losing momentum, initially gaining several points in a row through serves and winning the set. In the fourth set, Beiping immediately gained five points at the start with serves. Shandong's players were too eager to win, resulting in more out-of-bounds and self-inflicted errors. After the score reached 11-16, the momentum shifted completely, and Beiping won with a score of 21-11. (2) Rehe versus Hebei. The game was held at 3:30 PM. The first set was 22-20, with Rehe winning. The second set was 21-16, the third set was 21-19, and the fourth set was 21-11, all with Hebei winning. The overall result was 3-1, with Hebei securing the right to the final. The final against Beiping to compete for the championship will be held on the 14th. The intensity of this competition was no less than the Beiping-Shandong match. Rehe launched a fierce attack from the start, and Hebei resisted with all its strength. The scores increased alternately. However, in the fourth set, Rehe's players were unable to receive Hebei's high balls, and the back row was also unable to save dangerous balls, leading to their defeat.

Donghua Wins Opening Game, Defeats Xibu 5-2 204

Takes a 3-0 Lead in the First Half

Draws 2-2 in the Second Half

Yesterday was the second Sino-Western match since the opening of the Western League. The audience was shocked by the reputations of the Donghua and Xibu teams, and no fewer than 6,000 people went to watch. The Xibu team was far less brave and powerful than in the past. Their movements were slow, and their connection was also rigid and scattered. Although Yat Xu was heroic, his age was getting old, and his strength was not enough. Sometimes, he simply sighed at the ball. The first half ended with a score of 3-0. In the last quarter of an hour of the second half, they tried their best to counterattack, but they only scored two goals each. The result was a score of 5-2, with Xibu suffering a crushing defeat.

When center Dai Zhongfeng opened the scoring record, the golden bell reported three times. Xibu began to come slowly. The referee ordered the two armies to arrange their formations. Donghua kicked off not far away, and Yat Xu was invited to stop him. After a dozen rounds, Feng Yunyou rose up as a surprise soldier, took the ball into the enemy's formation, and transferred the ball to his home. Farlas Tao Ran came to grab it, and Jiaqiu was clever and took advantage of the situation to secretly hand it over to Lin Jing. He rode alone and flew to the doorstep, and shot fiercely at his feet. He fell into the net in response.

Cao Qiuting's Surprise Soldiers from Xieguzhong 205

Under the watchful eyes of thousands of people, the spirit of Donghua was greatly boosted, the iron cavalry was rampant, and the artillery was as rainy. Yat Xu mobilized his troops to defend and fought like trapped beasts. After a stalemate for five minutes, Jia Youliang rebelled on the frontier, killed the low line, and returned to the pass. Li Yichen was unusually cunning, bowing like this, letting the ball pass, and stabbing to see Cao Qiuting, a branch of the army descended from the sky, pulling up a leg, flat and rapid, Platley was caught off guard, and scurried into the net, clear, beautiful, and unwatchable.

Dai Lin Jing's Success on Top Once Again After that, the battlefield belonged to Donghua's world. Jia Youliang revisited his old place, and Cao Qiuting greeted him from the top. Fortunately, the enemy guard desperately patted it out, so that he could avoid it. Blayjack's disciples saw that they had lost two balls in an instant, and they all felt fire in their eyes and launched a major counterattack. Generals Li and Gu were as stable as rocks and as safe as Mount Tai. The door to the mainland was empty. Jia Youliang peeked for the third time and passed it into the dangerous area. Cao Qiuting topped to the right, and A Dai had been waiting for a long time, and entered the door by receiving the top, forming a score of three to zero, ending the first half.

The Injury of the Great General Gained One But Lost Two After a short break, the war started again. After Donghua adjusted its defense, its momentum did not weaken slightly. After the kick-off, Zeng Wuyi took the time, Feng Yunyou continued to transport military fire, Li Yichen took big steps and jumped out of the crowd, just a few feet away from the door, and he was about to succeed again. Zhejiang Provincial Government Allocates Funds to Aid Education in Various Counties 216

460,000 from Public Bonds

(Hangzhou News) Zhejiang Province has suffered from severe drought this summer, causing extremely heavy disasters. Tax revenues are insufficient, and sources of educational funding have been almost completely cut off. Various counties are in arrears with educational expenses, ranging from three or four days to as much as seven or eight months. The heads of various county education bureaus have jointly petitioned the provincial government one after another, requesting aid, seeking appropriations ranging from 150,000 to 200,000. The total requested appropriations from all eleven county education bureaus in the province amounts to nearly 2 million yuan. It has been learned that the Department of Education has agreed with the provincial government to allocate 460,000 yuan from the 20 million yuan public bond as loan funds for educational expenses in various counties.

Zhejiang Department of Education Orders Promulgation of Austerity Measures for Educational Expenses in Various Counties 218

Five Measures in Three Steps

(Hangzhou News) Zhejiang Province has suffered from drought this year, greatly affecting the income of educational expenses in various counties. Without strenuous efforts to tighten up various expenditures of county educational expenses this year, educational undertakings are likely to be brought to a standstill. In view of this, the Department of Education has carefully considered the importance and urgency of various educational undertakings in various counties and has drafted austerity measures for educational expenses in various counties for the 23rd year of the Republic. The basis for each county's austerity measures has already been distributed to various counties to handle according to the actual situation. The measures are excerpted below: (1) If the income of county educational expenses in the 23rd year is insufficient, the county should first try to maintain it. If it is impossible to list expenditures according to the original budget, it may be tightened in accordance with these measures. (2) The order of tightening up county educational expenses should proceed in the following three steps: A. First step austerity measures: include educational observation groups, trips to the province for meetings, investigation fees for vocational teachers, elementary education and folk education achievement exhibitions, children's activity gatherings, literacy campaigns, sports meets, etc. The originally listed expenses should be completely eliminated. B. Second step cumulative austerity measures: Educational institutions with few students and poor performance should merge classes or merge with nearby educational institutions of equivalent nature. The originally listed expenses should be completely eliminated or partially reduced. C. Third step austerity measures: Educational expenses for various educational institutions should be discounted and issued. The discount percentage, in addition to educational administrative agencies, should try to tighten their proportion as much as possible, with a larger percentage of 5% to 10% as the standard. Other institutions should follow a uniform principle. (3) If the county's educational expenses have been approved for reduction and austerity prior to the promulgation of these measures, they may still be handled as originally approved. (4) Counties with a smaller degree of educational expense shortfall should consider tightening the various expenses listed in the first step according to the actual situation of the county. (5) The austerity budget for county educational expenses should be submitted to the County Education and Education Committee for review and approval, and then submitted to the Department of Education for approval and implementation. These measures will be implemented after being announced by the Department of Education.

Meeting of Principals of Schools in the Urban Area Yesterday

Director Pan and More Than 30 Schools Including Wu Ben Attended

Soliciting Opinions from Various Schools on Guidance for Further Education and Employment

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education convened a meeting of principals of municipal middle schools and municipal elementary schools in the urban area at Wu Ben Girls' High School yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. Director Pan, Section Chief Zeng, Specialist Zhou, and more than 30 school principals attended. Details are recorded as follows:

Attending Principals 220

Including Wu Ben, Xin Lu, Wan Zhu, He An, Xi Cheng, Yang Zheng, Cang Ji, Shu Ji, Shi Hua, Xin Min, Fei Hong, Bi De, Cao Tang, Chao Zong, Zhongshan, Gao Chang, Ming Lun, Chong Zheng, Nan Qu, Mei Xi, Jiang Jing, Wei Da, Tan Zhen, Hui Qiao, Dong Ming, Peng Nan, Hong Dao, De Xin, Nan Xun, Nong Tan, and other more than 30 school principals Yan Zhenyu, Sheng Zhensheng, Gu Yinqian, Xu Shushen, Chai Zifei, Pan Dingyuan, Wang Dingcheng, Qian Xuanqing, Gu Jiwu, Jiang Menglin, Lu Huimin, and others.

Director's Report 221

First, Director Pan gave a report, stating that the purpose of convening the principals of municipal middle schools and municipal elementary schools in the Nanshi and Zhabei districts today is to solicit opinions from various schools on guiding students in further education and careers. The Shanghai Municipality's Measures for Guidance on Further Education and Careers for Elementary and Middle School Students have already been promulgated. Middle schools, starting from the second grade, and elementary schools, starting from the fifth grade, should all implement guidance on further education and careers in accordance with these measures. In addition to the establishment of a municipal committee for guidance on further education and careers by the Bureau of Education, each school should also have an organizational structure for the implementation of a committee for guidance on further education and careers. The number of committee members should be increased or decreased by each school depending on the circumstances, and the principal should be designated as a standing committee member. Each school already has this organization starting from this semester. At the second meeting of the Bureau of Education's committee for guidance on further education and careers, it was resolved that starting from the 13th academic year, the Bureau of Education would convene principals from various schools to solicit opinions in order to consider the actual situation and urge various schools to earnestly implement matters related to guidance on further education and careers for students within their schools. This is the purpose of today's meeting, and it is hoped that everyone will put forward any opinions they have as much as possible. Next, Section Chief Zeng briefly reported.

Schools' Opinions 222

Then, the principals of various schools successively reported on the implementation of guidance on further education and careers in their respective schools and expressed their opinions. The points are summarized as follows: (1) The curriculum of various elementary schools is often unable to connect, causing difficulties for elementary school graduates when taking middle school entrance examinations. Remedial measures should be sought. (2) Curriculum standards are not uniform, causing students to encounter difficulties in further education and examinations due to the different textbooks used by various schools. (3) The Bureau of Education should liaise with the industrial sector to have an organization for registration and job placement to facilitate the employment of students from various schools. The above points were handed over to the municipal committee for guidance on further education and careers for discussion. Finally, Director Pan gave instructions based on the reports of various schools, and the meeting adjourned at around 4:00 PM.

Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

The Most Difficult Subject 223

— Jun Si

Children, if someone asks you, "What is the most difficult subject?" I think you will definitely answer without hesitation, "It is arithmetic." Indeed, arithmetic is a subject that cannot be recited like Chinese, nor is it as easy to remember as general knowledge, so it often causes many children to be unable to solve problems, be punished by teachers, and develop a fear of arithmetic.

However, is arithmetic really the most difficult subject? This is probably not necessarily the case. If you approach arithmetic problems with an indomitable spirit, and if you can't solve it once, try again; if you can't solve it twice, keep trying. As long as you are a diligent child, no matter how difficult the problem is, you will eventually solve it, and the satisfaction of solving it with your own mind will bring you extra benefits and make you feel interested.

Arithmetic can be said to be the most important subject. All scientific inventions can be said to be based on arithmetic, so it has a great relationship to the strength or weakness of a country. Children, look! Our country is so weak, let's work hard on this most difficult subject.

Who Invented the Four Stationery Items? 224

— Ku

Children, who invented the pens, ink, paper, and inkstones that we use every day for writing? I'm afraid many students don't know the answer to this question. Let me tell you now:

Ink in our country was invented by Xing Yi of the Zhou Dynasty. Whether the ink at that time was graphite or glue ink is no longer possible to investigate, but pine soot ink only appeared in the Wei and Jin Dynasties, so the ink invented by Xing Yi was definitely not pine soot ink, which can be deduced. In addition, there are the inventors of the three items pen, paper and inkstone: one is Zhong You, a student of Confucius, who invented the stone inkstone; one is Meng Tian, a general during the Qin Dynasty, who invented the writing brush; and one is Cai Lun, a eunuch during the Eastern Han Dynasty, who invented paper.

Since they invented the stationery of our country, pen, ink, paper, and inkstone, it has become very convenient to write. At the same time, writing has gradually spread. We should thank them for their contributions to invention!

Tofu and Vegetables 225

— Rong Yu

When you children come to the dining table and see it full of chicken, duck, fish, and meat, you must be overjoyed. Those of you who are used to eating a bowl of rice with every meal will definitely want to add half a bowl or even a whole bowl. This truly embodies the idioms "wolfing down food" and "striving to eat more." But if today you see only tofu and vegetables on the table, you will definitely frown and lose your appetite. Naughty children will even cry and fuss with their parents. Children, do you usually have these habits?

Tofu and vegetables, you really shouldn't underestimate them. Their effects are actually better than those of fish and meat. This is because fish and meat only contain fats, which do not provide much nourishment for people. Moreover, sometimes they carry parasites, and eating them can cause illness. As for tofu, it is made from soybeans and contains abundant "vitamins," which are clean and nourishing. This has been generally recognized by people all over the world. The effects of vegetables are even greater. They also contain "vitamins." The "chlorophyll" in the leaves can also purify the blood and aid digestion. As long as they are cooked properly, the taste is no worse than fish and meat. Therefore, I advise you children to eat more vegetables and tofu every day.

The Relationship Between Expansion and Pressure 227

— Zhou Jiexin

Children, before you play with this experiment, you need to prepare a rice bowl, a teacup, a box of matches, and a piece of white paper -- about three and a half inches square.

First, pour a cup of water into the bowl, then crumple the paper into a ball, light it, and put it into the cup (note -- the cup should be dry). When it is about to burn out, immediately turn the cup upside down into the bowl. This way, you can see the water in the bowl gradually decreasing!

Children, think about it, what is the reason for this? The reason is very simple. When the burning paper is put into the bowl, the air in the cup expands due to heat and rises, and the pressure decreases. At that time, the inside of the cup can be considered a vacuum. When it is turned upside down in the bowl, because the air pressure outside is greater than the pressure inside the cup, it immediately forces the water into the cup!

Finally, we arrive at the following conclusion: The greater the expansion, the greater the decrease in pressure.

Common Knowledge of Raising Singing Insects 228

— Chi Fo

In autumn, there are many singing insects in front of the steps and among the flowers. Crickets, katydids, gold crickets, and "Guo Guo Er" all have very pleasant singing voices, and children all like to keep them in cages.

Swallows come in the spring; geese leave in the spring: these are called "migratory birds." Insects chirp and sing in the autumn, so they are also called "migratory insects." This is also a characteristic of animals.

Crickets are naturally brave and like to fight. The winner often flaps its wings and sings. Children often like to keep them in bamboo cages to watch them fight. When I was young, I kept crickets in earthenware jars. I made several holes in the mud inside the jar for the crickets to live in, like the cave-dwelling life of ancient times. With this method of raising them, crickets could often be kept until winter. "Ji Ling," "Ji Ling," admiring their singing.

Katydids are also known as "spinning girls" because their chirping sounds like spinning. They live among flowers and plants, are small and green, and chirp loudly. Sitting in the autumn courtyard at night, it sounds like a sudden gust of wind and heavy rain. Children only need to lure them from a distance with a lamp, and they will definitely fly over, making it easy to catch them. Just feed them pumpkin flowers and red water chestnut meat, and they will be able to live and sing to you at night.

"Guo Guo Er," also called "Call Brother," is an autumn insect produced in the corn, millet, and millet plants in the Jiangbei region. They are caught and kept in cages made of fine bamboo strips and sold in the streets, making it easy for children to buy them. "Call Brother" chirps and sings all day long, which is annoying. Crickets and gold crickets are better because they are quiet and pleasant to listen to.

Gold crickets are small and golden, and they are a petite and exquisite autumn insect. But its chirping is very loud. They live in clumps of bamboo and shrubs. We put a bamboo basket below and use a wooden stick to beat the clumps of bamboo and shrubs. The gold crickets will fall into the basket, and we can catch them. The cage for raising gold crickets can be made of glass; or it can be made in the style of a clock, or in the style of a pagoda -- octagonal, rectangular, or round -- all of which can be made by oneself. This is also a child's craft. When I was young, I really liked making them myself. Gold crickets only eat some rice grains, and they don't need much food. If they are raised properly, they can still live through the winter, but the chirping will be very faint. At this time, they should be kept in a warm room with cotton wadding inside the cage so that they won't freeze to death. I remember one year, when the weather was already cold, I was afraid that they would freeze to death, so I exposed them to the sun. Who knew that the time was too long, and they all died in the sun. Because they were trapped in the cage, they couldn't escape, and they all died. "Loving them ended up harming them." Children! There are many such things!

Fairy Tale 229

— Written by Ms. Qin Qianpei

(1) Naughty three brothers, playing by the river, saw something swimming in the river. They had never seen it before, so they thought it must be a monster, and threw stones at it. (2) The monster cried out in panic, and they laughed and prepared to leave. (3) The monster stood up heroically, and they were so frightened that they ran for their lives.

Two Scientific Toys 230

— Dun

The parachute used on airplanes is an extremely fashionable and scientific toy that can be experimented with.

Children, in your spare time, you may wish to try making one. If there are many people, you can hold a competition to see who flies higher or lower, which will add to the fun.

First, make an arrow shaft out of wood, then take a larger handkerchief, and tie the four corners to the arrow shaft with thread. However, the lines should be longer, and the length of each line should be the same to avoid tilting when landing.

Take another wooden strip and tie a rope to it. Tie a knot at the end of the rope to make a launcher. When launching, hook the knot of the rope into the pre-cut notch on the arrow shaft. Hold the arrow shaft with your left hand and the launcher with your right hand. Swing the launcher into the air with your right hand, and immediately release the arrow shaft with your left hand. The parachute will fly into the air (Figure 1).

Lightweight Clock: Take a larger wooden box, and drill a round "匚" hole on each of the left and right sides. Draw the hour markings on one side (Figure 2). Then take a wooden rod that fits the size of the round hole to assemble the hour hand. Place an empty thread spool between the two round holes. Place a thin hemp thread on the spool. Tie a piece of tinplate to one end and a piece of "Wen" wood to the other end. (The weight of the tinplate and the wood should be equal.) Use an empty cigarette can below, drill a small "匚" hole, fill it with water, and float the wood on the surface of the water (Figure 2). Assemble it, and put the cigarette can on another can to hold water. It can be used.

Because the water in the "云" tube drips down from the "一" hole, the wood lowers along with the surface of the water, pulling the round shaft, and the needle on the outside rotates at the same time (Figure 3).

Brush 231

— (Ge Shoumin, Minsheng Girls' Elementary School)

A brush is something made of pig bristles and cattle bones, and it is used to remove dirt. If there were no such thing in the world, people would feel uncomfortable and unclean. Uncleanliness would affect people's health, and the unsound bodies of the people would cause society, the country, and even the world to lack spirit and vitality. Therefore, although a brush is a small thing, it has such great importance to people.

Since brushes are so useful, is there not a large brush that can remove the uncleanliness of the country and wash away the national shame? Yes, the large brush for washing away national shame is not something made of pig bristles and cattle bones. It is naturally created, and it is the pair of hands and a brain that each of us has.

Compatriots! Quickly rise up! Use our naturally created large brushes, our brains and hands, to wash away our country's extraordinary shame!

Children of the World 232

— Wen Yuyang

(I) The children of the Native Americans have completely different ways of playing games than we do. They often play archery, and they are very good at it, so good you could say they hit the bullseye every time. Because they make a living by hunting and fishing, they must practice the skills necessary for life in childhood.

(II) Swiss children often carry a stick, a knapsack, and wear shoes with spiked soles when they go out to play. The stick and shoes help them climb mountains or cross water, and the knapsack contains raincoats and shirts for rain and changes in the weather. This is also to adapt to the climate and environment.

(III) In Philippine schools, most of their buildings are made of palm trees and bamboo. The students there have very short hair that stands straight up like bristles. They also wear the bottom half of their shirts outside their pants, and wear slippers on their feet, which is not very attractive.

(IV) Dutch children mostly wear wooden shoes. We find them clumsy and heavy, but in the Netherlands, where the land is low and there is a lot of water, wearing these shoes is most suitable.

P Teaching Songs 233

— Yan Banguang

Old-fashioned song lyrics are being phased out with the evolution of the times, like; Eighteen Touches, Rowing a Boat on the Lake, and the like. The newly popular song lyrics are surging like the tides, like; Peach Blossom River is a Beauty's Nest, Lullaby, and the like. Many young girls are frantically learning to sing.

Mrs. Huang across the street has been working hard to teach three young girls to sing. My house and her house face each other, and my long window happens to face her hexagonal window opening. Every morning, or when it is quiet in the evening, Mrs. Huang uses a very clumsy method to teach singing. She bought a record player, first copied down the lyrics on the record, had them read them until they were familiar, and then told them to sing along with the record player. But people's aptitude varies between clever and stupid. Mrs. Huang doesn't care, she only knows to whip them with a leather whip if they can't sing, beating them while constantly saying; "Dumb fool! Stupid thing!" with loud shouts and beatings.

Sometimes in the early morning or late at night, I am always awakened by the crying and shouting. I open the window to look and can still see streaks of purple marks under the light of the sixteen electric lamps. I also hear Mrs. Huang saying that she is doing it for their own good, that she is beating them so they can become famous! After several days of investigation, I learned that these three girls are not Mrs. Huang's own daughters, so no wonder she can use such vicious methods every day, and it is really not easy for Chinese singers to become famous!

How the Moon Was Formed 234

— Bing Yu

The moon that we see every night gradually becomes full from the first night to the fifteenth night of the lunar calendar, and then gradually wanes from the sixteenth night to the thirtieth night, in an endless cycle throughout the year. But how was this moon formed? It is really strange and incredible. Now I will tell you one theory of how it was formed; A scholar said that tens of millions of years ago, a part of the Earth we live on separated from the Earth and became the Moon. However, is this theory ultimately reliable? We cannot be sure, but when we investigate the shape of the Earth tens of millions of years ago, it was not like it is now, with land, sea, and animals and plants, but a chaotic, huge mass of gas. Therefore, famous scientists such as George Darwin and Henri Poincaré of France, from the standpoint of mathematics, studied the Earth in the era of this gas mass and obtained an equation for how it became the Moon. That is to say, in the era of the gas mass, the Earth had a very fast base spinning force, and as a result of the spinning, its shape became elliptical (oval). Later, the gas mass gradually cooled and became a large mass of liquid (that is, a part of the Earth, because of the spinning and vibration, a small mass occurred. This small mass gradually grew like a tumor, and later, under the influence of centrifugal force and solar force fluctuations, it suddenly separated from the large mass and existed independently in the air. This is the reason for the birth of the Moon. The volume of this moon is 5,000 cubic miles. According to the research of astronomers, the place where the Moon separated from the Earth is the mark of the separation of the small mass and the large mass, which is on the Pacific side. However, this theory was overturned by Dr. Archenhold, because according to Dr. Archenhold's opinion, he said: If we simply calculate, the volume of the seabed of the Pacific Ocean is less than one-thirtieth of the volume of the Moon. Even if we gather the world's three major oceans, the Pacific Ocean, the Atlantic Ocean, and the Indian Ocean, they are not as large as the Moon. In the end, the theory that the Moon was separated from the Earth is established, but its traces must not be on the Pacific side. According to astronomical calculations and investigations, the average distance from the Earth to the Moon is 384,400 kilometers. To travel to the Moon once, at the current rate of regular air travel, calculated by passenger planes traveling 150 kilometers per hour, it would take 107 days to reach the Moon. If calculated by the special express train of the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway, it would take more than 250 or 60 days. As for how big the Moon is, according to detailed investigations by astronomers, it is one-fiftieth of the Earth, with a diameter of 3,476 kilometers. On the Moon, half of each month is daytime and half is nighttime, unlike the Earth, which has an atmosphere and a hydrosphere, so the temperature changes on the Moon are very drastic. During the day, it receives heat from the sun, and at night, the heat it receives from the sun completely disappears. That is, the temperature can be over a hundred degrees Celsius during the day, reaching as high as 180 degrees during the full moon, and suddenly dropping to hundreds of degrees below zero at night. The dark, low-lying areas will also drop to 180 degrees below zero, so no living things can survive. In terms of the brightness of the moon; there are 4 billion lights, the most terrible thing is that there are craters of dead volcanoes everywhere, all desolate, with some things left behind. In recent years, astronomers and explorers from various countries have often thought about traveling to the Moon, but because of the long distance, the rapid changes in temperature, and the air conditions, they dare not take the risk. If the Moon's surroundings also develop a hydrosphere and atmosphere in the future, then life can occur. Judging from this, the saying in our country's legend that Emperor Xuanzong of Tang traveled to the Moon Palace is completely absurd and unfounded.

American Cotton Maintained Due to Price Increase Theory 246

A telegram from New York on October 11th reported on the cotton market for the week: At the beginning of the week, the cotton market was actively covering shorts because the government's cotton production estimate was slightly smaller than expected. However, general buying sentiment did not develop as a result. Subsequently, the market weakened due to continued liquidation by various parties, especially those from overseas. In addition, the Marseille tragedy occurred, and selling became rampant. Before long, European news stabilized sentiment, and market prices rose sharply. Liquidation gradually subsided, and short covering also increased. The strong performance of the stock and wheat markets also contributed to the improvement in the cotton market. The authorities have a better attitude towards commercial news, and President Roosevelt has also proposed his idea of raising prices. The theory of inflation has also been spread again for a time, so the general opinion is that once the various parties have completed their liquidation, the futures price will not necessarily be lower than the government's price for cotton collection and loan issuance. The reason why the various parties have been liquidating recently is that their anticipated inflation ideal has not been realized, and they are inevitably disappointed. Moreover, the stability of the US dollar and the government's cotton loan program have failed to maintain the rising trend, so they are panic-stricken. The cotton cloth market has been quiet this week, but reports of separate sales transactions are still good.

Grain and Flour Market Turns from Weak to Stable 247

Yesterday, the flour market showed a trend of first falling and then stabilizing in each month after the opening. Foreign wheat quotations in Chicago were closed for the holiday, and Canada fell back by about 50 to 60 cents, so when the prices opened, the near and far term markets were weak, falling by 1 to 1.5 cents compared to the closing price of the previous day. Subsequently, as factories threw out stock, most still took a wait-and-see approach, while off-market short positions were slightly covered, so opening prices resumed stability. Until the afternoon opening, near-term sentiment was flat, while the far-term was stable. However, because a warship sailed to Tianjin with an estimated 50,000 bags, delivering to Tianjin at only 2 yuan, 3 jiao, and 1.5 fen, a portion of the standard market covered their shorts, and the market showed good movement. According to industry speculation, factories throw out stocks. Half must be based on whether foreign wheat is profitable, and half must be based on the exchange's restoration of substitutes before it can be lively as usual. As a result, this month was better by 7.5%, November was better by 1%, December was better by 5%, January was better by 1.2%, and February was better by 1.5%.

Yesterday, the wheat futures market showed a trend of being initially flat and then stable in each month after the opening in the morning and afternoon. Foreign wheat quotations in Chicago and Canada fell back by about 50 to 60 cents. The market was flat when it first opened in the morning, with little change compared to the previous day. Later, as the flour market turned stable, sentiment also stabilized. Until the afternoon opening, trading in each month was still exceptionally quiet, but there were very few sellers, and the flour market felt like it was turning active again, so market sentiment in each month improved slightly again. Currently, the rise and fall of the wheat market depends purely on the flour market. In the future, the pricing of foreign wheat will still have an inevitable connection with the future of domestic wheat. As a result, this month was better by 4%, November was better by 1%, December was better by 3%, January was better by 2%, and February was better by 2%. The spot wheat market remained quiet because factory demand was weak and prices were not starting.
