Women's Corner

Abortion and Contraception 256

— Fortunately

Since Mr. Zi Jiu published the article "Abortion" in issue 31 of this publication, followed by Mr. Zhou Shazi's response to the article, "A Review of Remedial Abortion," in issue 33, it is clear that abortion has become a matter of general public attention. It is no longer the case that those involved act in secrecy and stealth, while bystanders remain dismissive and indifferent, as in the past.

Mr. Zi Jiu pointed out the motives for abortion as: (1) being burdened by economic hardship and unable to afford upbringing; (2) being dedicated to a career, thereby avoiding the trouble of raising children; (3) being physically weak and unable to withstand childbirth; (4) becoming pregnant out of wedlock, fearing social stigma, or having no one to take responsibility. Mr. Shazi added another item: "All patients with mental illnesses, severe tuberculosis patients, etc., should be obliged to control childbirth or have abortions." It can be said that the reasons, significance, and value of "abortion" have been explained in great detail. Here, I only want to briefly discuss other reasons that the two gentlemen overlooked in their writings, and the issue of contraception that is associated with the "abortion" problem.

To begin, regarding abortion, I believe that in addition to the above items, it also has considerable value in other ways, namely: (1) stopping childbearing when the appropriate number of children has been reached, and (2) reducing the risks and complications of broken romances during the initial period of cohabitation. I will now elaborate as follows:

(1) This is a problem that is related to many aspects, including family finances, family education, female physiology, children's well-being, and the health of the race. Usually, it is not uncommon for a woman to conceive seven or eight times, or even more than ten times. If they are allowed to be born naturally, then due to the frequency of childbirth, the family's finances will be in a very difficult situation, the mother's body will be greatly depleted, and the later-born children will inevitably be weaker than their older sisters and brothers. Furthermore, the parents' limited energy will make it even more difficult to cope with the education, life, and even daily matters such as sleep, clothing, and food for this large number of children. In that case, how can we talk about children's well-being and the health of the race? Therefore, when there are already many children, childbirth should be stopped artificially, while maintaining normal sexual activity between the two sexes. To achieve these two points, in addition to active contraception, we must rely on passive abortion.

(2) This is a key factor in many divorce cases that are currently being discovered. Due to the deep-rooted concept of individualistic and sacred love, marriage is based on this. However, love that rises too quickly often collapses easily, especially when children are born too early, preventing the mother from working outside the home and increasing the family's burden, leading to economic reasons. Thus, the sacred theory of love, which previously promoted the union, is now used as a reason for divorce. However, at this time, the small child becomes an obstacle to the freedom of both parties to separate, and some even reluctantly maintain a painful life because of it. This is the biggest obstacle between divorced couples, and at the same time, it is a great sacrifice for the child. Therefore, in order to ensure that they do not have children in the first few years of marriage, wait until a suitable amount of time has passed, both parties are confident that the love can last, and the family's finances are not difficult, and then have the children they need. Or, if unfortunately, both parties feel dissatisfied and can divorce decisively, without the burden of children or the disputes over alimony, in addition to implementing contraception from the beginning, abortion is a necessary measure.

Then, I will proceed to talk about "contraception." This has been mentioned from time to time in the above text, and it has also been mentioned several times in Mr. Shazi's article. "It is best to use various reasonable birth control methods before conception, which is a fundamental solution," which is especially clear and accurate. However, because it was written with a focus on abortion, it has not been deeply analyzed. Personally, I feel that one is a prevention before the event, and the other is a remedy after the event. In comparison, the importance of contraception actually exceeds that of abortion.

There are several reasons for this:

First, in terms of procedure, contraception only requires a little preparation before intercourse, which is an easy task; while abortion, even if the Chinese health authorities have allowed you to openly request it, or there are "reasonable artificial abortion clinics or consulting offices" established, it is still very troublesome. Moreover, at present, society does not publicly allow abortion, not to mention those who mistakenly send their lives to unlicensed midwives and drugs. Even if there are a few skilled surgeons, they either do things in a complicated way or take the opportunity to extort money. The unpleasantness in between can be imagined, not to mention the economic conditions that are attached?

Second, in terms of economic conditions, everything in society is inseparable from the economic foundation. Whether it is contraception or abortion, economics is indeed the most important of all reasons. In order to stop childbearing because of the unbearable burden of life, using contraception methods, the cost is of course limited. But the surgeon's fee for an abortion is very high (of course, this may be different when there is a public institution). Originally, in order to reduce the burden, is this temporary expenditure not enough to stump the poor? Like the woman from Wuxi, Yu Yang, who paid 70 yuan for the abortion fee and was fined 80 yuan by the police, I really feel sorry for her.

Third, in terms of women's health, the need for contraception or abortion is mostly due to physical weakness and the inability to bear the pain of childbirth, then the former is naturally the safest and most convenient method. Abortion, even in very early months, is almost like a miscarriage, which will harm the body to some extent; especially for those who are already weak and sick, to have an abortion, the degree of loss is more serious than natural childbirth. Moreover, according to general experience (perhaps with more theoretical basis), artificial abortion can actually promote conception.

The meaning of comparing contraception and abortion above is only to clearly indicate that contraception is more reasonable, more necessary, and more practical to promote than abortion in fact. If it is "a foregone conclusion", abortion is naturally still a remedial measure; but we must remember that this is only a post-remedial measure!

In short, from all aspects, especially from the economic, women's liberation, and physiological perspectives, abortion does have a value to be established, and contraception is especially necessary to promote.

As for how to practice contraception, this is a practical scientific question, which should rely on the discussion and introduction of legitimate doctors and researchers in this field.

The Work of Modern Soviet Women (Continued) 257

— Translated by Xue Jihui

By Miss M.E. Walker

The medical profession also attracts many women. In the past, only men studied this profession. Now, according to the professors in various universities, the majority of medical students are women. One professor told me very firmly that two-thirds of his students are female. This professor may be an enthusiast for women. I have pleasant memories of talking with female doctors and nurses in Russia. There are many unsung heroes among both types of workers. One young woman, recently certified as qualified, invited me one morning to her small wooden house, two hundred miles from the city. Her working area extends sixty miles east and forty miles west of her residence. Her only means of transportation is a horse or a springless farm cart. She lives a very simple life there alone, with only the most common medicines. While busy treating diseases, setting bones, pulling teeth, and assisting in childbirth, she also takes care of three types of serious illnesses: pneumonia, malaria, and meningitis. She puts these three patients in a room in her small wooden house, which she calls "my hospital." In the evenings, she spends all her time lecturing to the villagers on hygiene, first aid, cleanliness, and prevention of tuberculosis, etc.

At a certain university, I met a team of female medical students, many of whom were working and studying at the same time. They used their spare time to set up a sanatorium in the school for those classmates who were malnourished or unhealthy. They also set up a cafeteria, providing the most hygienic food at the lowest prices. They maintained this work for three years, even though they had to get up at five o'clock every morning to prepare breakfast. They felt that this was simply a responsibility they owed to their comrades.

One day, I spoke with nurses at a certain hospital and learned that they were connected with several social service organizations that I had known before. She specializes in visiting families, especially in densely populated areas of large cities. She reports all hygienic shortcomings, infectious diseases, and unsanitary conditions. Their work has many similarities to our social service work, but their authority is much greater. No family, factory, shop, or public place can escape their supervision. One of the greatest panic of their work: is the movement to ban prostitution, ban alcohol, and eliminate superstition. A team of female workers, in order to promote the temperance movement, organized public cafeterias everywhere so that workers could get good food and drinks under their management. They said this was a fundamental way to eradicate drinking, and they would continue to work hard until the bad habit of drinking was completely eliminated. They argued for the elimination of the burden of housework that binds women on the grounds of gender equality; because this burden is enough to prevent women from serving the country and other jobs.

Those nurses I mentioned above also told me that they would be the vanguard in the anti-illiterate midwife movement among the Tartar people. During the preparation period, they not only had to learn a foreign language, but also had to prepare lectures on various social issues, methods of preventing diseases, and even teach people to read and write. Many women are engaged in this work; among this small nation, many people still live a nomadic life, and they naturally oppose others interfering with their long-standing way of life. They believe that women's liberation is a catastrophe that they need to put out by all means. However, the germ of women's freedom has penetrated deep into their tribes. Those women are eagerly accepting it. Some have even removed their veils and come out to study, or even become representatives in the National Assembly. These women return to cooperate with personnel sent from Moscow, Leningrad, or Kharkov to do advocacy work. They feel that women in these backward nations need the ability to live independently in order to achieve freedom and liberation. Therefore, they improved family industries and peasant industries based on appropriate business principles. In some places, they restored various crafts that had long been forgotten.

Regarding the medical field, I also observed another situation: women can do medical research work. I found that the director of a large microbiology academy, Montessori (Montessori) P · N · E · U several systems, and not like any one. Those children are certainly very happy, full of many meanings, often expressed in sand piles, perforated paper, or loess. Outsiders may find it strange how our country catches and punishes those who engage in speculative activities and commit crimes—they are usually subjected to severe penalties—but there is no secret. A large team of women specializes in this work. They mix with the shoppers in the vegetable market or on busy streets in the city. While shopping, they pay close attention to everyone passing by. They are very familiar with all the tricks of fraud, especially those that harm the interests of the state. Therefore, these behaviors rarely escape their keen observation. They are obviously the great enemies of deceivers; if they find fraudulent behavior, they will be severely punished. If the defrauded is a worker, they will be dealt with even more severely. If the person taking advantage is not a worker in the narrow sense, their punishment will be even more severe.

Talking About Crying 258

— Bi Wu

Last year we talked about domestic goods, but in a country that relies on agriculture and in a year of good harvest, we still imported large quantities of foreign rice and foreign wheat. This year we talked about women, but women have become even more confined to the home, becoming prostitutes, and being reduced to maids and concubines. Talking is indeed only talking! But there is nothing to say, so we still have to talk.

It has always been thought that women "are good at crying": in ancient times, there was the wife of Hua Zhou Qiliang, who cried for her husband for ten days, and the city wall collapsed; in recent times, there were female students from Beiping Peiman School, who gathered to cry all day long on "September 18," without eating or drinking. It seems that this saying is quite true. But Shen Baoxu cried at the Qin court for seven days and seven nights, and Ruan Ji cried over the road to ruin, who knows how many times in his life. These men are also crying men.

Those who suffer and endure hardship and have unspeakable pain in their hearts cannot help but wail. When the Northeast was first lost, hundreds of thousands of people across the country surrounded the government and cried bitterly, surrounding the mausoleum of Sun Yat-sen and crying bitterly. The capital was filled with wailing. Now that the three years of mourning have ended, there is still a final scene of female students gathering and crying in Beiping.

Family members cry for those who have been devastated and harmed; the people cry for the country that has been invaded and annexed. Only those like the wife of Chen Huasheng, who sells herself into prostitution to maintain her husband's livelihood, but finally cannot be tolerated and is killed by her husband; no one in society sheds tears for such people, and even their close relatives, such as their maternal uncles, avoid asking and hearing about it. This corner has become a place without tears.

Silently enduring devastation and oppression, from pain to death, without receiving a single tear from people, such people are filling the society. Just looking at the women's side, the evil diseases entangled with prostitutes, the unhealthy development of maids, the hardships endured by wives and concubines—these things have generally been regarded as natural. Things that are taken for granted do not need pity.

Where does this "natural" view come from? Needless to say, it is the crystallization of politics, law, etiquette, customs, and all the ideas of respecting men and despising women. The hearts of society have been stirred by thousands of years of thought like paste, and hundreds of thousands of people have fallen into it, without causing ripples or reactions. For the sake of the oppressed, especially the oppressed women, this is the most worthy place to cry bitterly.

Crying for one person's experience, crying for the devastation of one family, is not even the sound of ants in society. It is necessary to connect with millions of people who shed tears in secret before it can be hoped to become a roar. Shout down the old ideas, old morals, old systems, and everything that is broken and incomplete and unable to cope with today's serious oppression of imperialism in this society that is dead and confused.

Once confined to the family, she does not know the greatness of society, but only cries for the insignificance of herself. This will continue with her great-great-grandmother and even her great-great-granddaughter, crying endlessly. The so-called women "are good at crying" actually becomes especially not good at crying.

Child Rearing 259

— Yao Fei

China started women's schools in 1907 (the 33rd year of the Guangxu reign) and has been doing so until now. It can be said that it has spent money on the education of "virtuous mothers and good wives". Even now, female students in various universities are still learning "domestic affairs" courses! However, speaking of the effect, it is extremely pitiful; may I ask, who has seen a few typical virtuous mothers and good wives? And who can stand up and say, "I am worthy of the title of virtuous mother and good wife without any guilt"? There is no doubt that it is a complete failure. This is not accidental: First, the educated people, at least the middle-class women, have nothing to do with the general public, that is, the majority of workers and peasants; secondly, these educated women marry into middle-class families and spend their days calling servants and maids. If they have children, they are handed over to wet nurses. Their only task is to provide entertainment! And they themselves, aware of the fact that "love fades as beauty fades," naturally use all their energy to dress up and decorate themselves! Needless to say, this group of people has formed a life view of being a doll, and they are not virtuous mothers and good wives at all. As for marrying into middle-class families, the family life habits are completely opposite to those in school. The seven things to open the door, the domestic affairs textbooks are not enough to deal with, and production and child rearing cannot be begged for lectures! So they respectfully accept the traditional family style and habits, or they are lazy and do nothing, and everything is ignored. So everything "remains the same"! So we constantly hear criticisms like "the bad effects after liberation". In fact, the women's education in the past was only regarded as decoration by those who ran it, and those who studied it only did it to catch up with fashion. Both the teachers and the students ignored the principle of "being a person": (occasional successful or awakened women were not the power of school education). It can be seen that the women's education in the past was not based on the education of "people" with the principle of equality between men and women! Moreover, the public establishment of women's schools only focused on families above the middle class, and those who went to receive education were all women with money and leisure. As for the working, peasant, and poor masses, their food and clothing were deprived, so what are we talking about women's education!

"Ignoring everything about the children and letting them be natural," no one has ever advocated this. However, phenomena such as "poor people's children wandering around the streets with disheveled hair and dirty faces, and rich people's children wandering around at home in a charming and delicate way, and when they grow up, they all wander around in society in a confused and dark way, the same as their fathers, or even worse," can this kind of phenomenon be solved by the virtuous mother and good wife doctrine? However, this is still a phenomenon in 1918 (see "Hot Wind"), and now it is still it, or even worse.

There are also people who know how to cherish children, or who intend to raise children according to the theory of child-centeredness, but in the family, it is certainly impossible to do it in a large family. Even in a small family, it is still a fantasy. I remember "The Family of Retribution" (see "Wandering") which describes a pair of newlyweds with ideals, but the whip of life made the heroine lose her courage and the smile on her face, leaving a irritable temper and a pair of gloomy eyes. She often beat the child until he cried! And the master also failed to work because of this, and often got up to tease the child (such as doing "cat washing face," etc.), ":: I am afraid that in the future it will be five five twenty-five, nine nine eighty-one! :: And two eyes are gloomy::" His sad mood makes people feel disappointed! Another example is an article "Children" in "Back View", which is Zhu Ziqing writing about his own situation with his children. It is not that he does not understand the philosophy and ethics of raising children, nor is it that he does not know the loveliness of children, only because the children will quarrel and make noise, making him "If I sit at home reading or writing something, I will have to be distracted several times in an hour, or stand up once or twice. If it is a rainy day or a Sunday, and the children are at home a lot, then, I can't read a line after opening a book, and I can't write a word when I pick up a pen:::". So he "still deals with it barbarically according to the ancient tradition, like ordinary fathers"::: "Corporal punishment and scolding"! He even said in a letter to Sheng Tao, "The torment of children is really helpless; sometimes I even feel that suicide is better." Although he later shed tears for these and cried a lot.

The above are seen from books, let's talk about a current event; a certain gentleman, the current director of the Department of Education of a certain national university, is a child psychology expert himself, and his wife is a professional talent who graduated from a women's higher normal school. He took several biological children and lived in the new village of the professor environment. This kind of family, this kind of parents, this kind of environment, should be ideal! However, the children's experience is no exception to the general one; beating and scolding cannot be avoided! The reason is nothing more than that the children are noisy, restless, and hinder work, and so on.

Based on the examples cited above, it can be seen that the family is not a paradise for children, and it is not enough to bear the responsibility of good nurturing and education. The truth of the new-style families of the middle and upper-middle-class intellectuals is like this, and the general working, peasant, and poor families are even more what we can see everywhere we open our eyes! It can be seen that "bearing the responsibility of educating new children," even the new-style families of intellectuals, are not worthy of it.

The general prejudice is that direct parents are more fond of their children than others, and they cannot rest assured to hand them over to others. And people with well-developed maternal instincts especially cannot bear to leave their children by themselves. In fact, we all have emotions and reason. "Love your young ones and extend it to the young ones of others," "Treat your compatriots as your own," and humans have not only had this kind of thinking since now - it is even more developed now! Also, love; and how to love? are two things! Education; and how to educate well? are also two things! For children, what is considered to be able to love reasonably - not to fall into doting, and loving them is just to harm them - to educate, how can we educate in the right way - so that they are happy and prosperous, and both body and spirit can be healthy! We should always take care of this. Besides, the more important point is; in the past, people generally regarded children as their own possessions - property, mostly having raising without education. Even if they taught, it was only to honor the ancestors and make the family prosperous! There were very few parents who made them become "national scholars". Now; whether we regard children as members of the country or cells of humanity, at least we should not make them "take the family as the world | as the universe" anymore! May I ask, can even the most ideal family be competent for this kind of education? Should we not now transfer the responsibility of nurturing and educating children from the family to the society? We have emotions and reason, we should make children become members who adapt to or create a new society - and never make them consistently belong to the boils of the family again!

General Life of Women in Shantou 260

— Peng Yujiong

(Shantou Correspondence)

I arrived in Shantou a week ago, intending to conduct a more detailed and comprehensive observation of the general living conditions of women here. That is why I am only now able to pick up my pen.

The first thing we must acknowledge about the women here is that they are healthy. The various labels of "morbid beauty" and "Oriental beauty" are simply inapplicable to them.

(1) Women in Schools || The majority of female students in schools here are quite healthy and simple. However, in a Chinese society heavily shrouded in feudal ideas, we have never seen a place, whether it be an institution or a school, where men and women enjoy equal development. Shantou is no exception.

With the global economic panic sweeping over us, the sluggishness of the Shantou market is obviously apparent to us. Under immense pressure, most of the women in Shantou have been driven back to their families, with no further opportunity to enjoy the benefits of school education! Consequently, the number of women in schools here is indeed very small!

(2) Women in Families || The habit of not treating women as equals, which has persisted for thousands of years, is still deeply ingrained here! Aside from a small number of upper-class women who can spend their days at home doing nothing, living the life of a young mistress or young lady, most women in families have to toil in the homes of ordinary people, performing arduous household chores!

What is particularly noteworthy here is that in some relatively affluent families, they often employ several poor girls under the age of ten as "maids." They work tirelessly every day until they are nearly sixteen or seventeen years old, when they become adults. At this point, the male head of the household, regardless of whether he is gray-haired or over ninety years old, will take these teenage maids to satisfy their "sexual desires," ostensibly elevating them to the status of "concubine"! In reality, they remain in the position of "maid," with no rights to enjoy in the family, because there are still several layers of powerful figures above them – the so-called first wife and other concubines! I have noticed this phenomenon particularly in the Guangdong area. Therefore, the practice of taking "maids" as concubines is seen as commonplace in Guangdong. As a result, can't we see that the women in the so-called South, who loudly proclaim the tide of women's liberation, are in such a pitiful situation?

(3) Women in Rural Areas || Under the extremely bankrupt state of the countryside, the vast majority of women in the South have no choice but to flock to the cities to find a way to make a living. Some, although unable to move to the city, still lead very difficult lives in the countryside. When we were coming south from Shanghai, as the ship approached the dock, I couldn't distinguish between men and women. Wearing straw hats, bent over, and barefoot, they carried heavy loads on the road. Finally, a friend told me that these were poor rural women carrying grain or vegetables to sell in the city! There are also many fruit stalls on the streets run by women. In short, most of the women in Shantou are productive, healthy, and simple, but they are also very impoverished and struggling to live under dual oppression.

An Interview with the Shanghai Jiliang Institute 261

— Wu

It was an afternoon with the autumn wind blowing and teeth chattering. I went alone to the Shanghai Jiliang Institute on Niuzhuang Road.

The surroundings were filled with a strong Christian atmosphere. The walls were hung with illustrations from the Bible. The doors were plastered with Jesus' commandments. From next door came the hymns sung by the children of the institute's affiliated free primary school.

While waiting to be received, I was almost forced to suffocate. Ten minutes passed before a kind-looking elderly believer, Ms. Kong, appeared at the door inside.

According to her own introduction, she was in charge of management responsibilities. So, we opened the conversation with mutual modesty.

"First, please tell me about the general situation of your institute," I said first.

Ms. Kong thought for a moment and replied, "The institute's regular expenses are four thousand per month, mostly sourced from fundraising by the board of directors from the church. Although the patrol room and the Public Security Bureau provide monthly subsidies, the amount is small.

The organization of the institute is now divided into three parts: (1) Adults: that is, the women's section. (2) Children: referring to minors. (3) Hospital: This is specifically for treating illnesses of women or children in the institute. However, sometimes outsiders are also treated. In short, it is all charitable in nature.

Their daily lives in the women's section are as follows: Breakfast at 7:00 AM. Classes from 8:00 AM to 12:00 PM. Lunch after class. Sleep from 1:00 PM to 2:00 PM in the afternoon. Handicrafts, such as embroidery and sewing, are taught from 2:00 PM to 4:00 PM. Stroll after 4:00 PM. Dinner at 6:00 PM. Night study from 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM. Lights out at 9:00 PM. As for the children's section, it is exactly the same as a regular primary school, with full-day classes.

Currently, there are about six hundred people in the entire institute, with adult women accounting for about two-thirds of them.

"What are the main reasons they come to the institute? Are there any who come to request admission on their own?" I asked after she finished the above.

"The reasons for coming to the institute are mostly because they were 'sold' or 'abused.' After a court judgment, they are all sent here. Therefore, there were quite a few prostitutes in the institute in the past. Of course, there are also those who come to request admission on their own, but we rarely accept them. In fact, in such a large city as Shanghai, if we were to help everyone, we would be overwhelmed."

"What kind of books do they read?"

"The books they read are mostly books that encourage people to do good. The Bible is the main subject. The reason is very simple: our food is given to us by God, so naturally we should absolutely believe in God, right?" Ms. Kong said with unusual excitement. At the same time, she pointed to the sky, as if telling people that God lived there.

"Is the education in the women's section equivalent to that of primary school?"

"The institute only goes up to the primary school level, but if there are promising girls, the institute can ask the church to provide them with secondary school education, even university education. However, this right is not available to women. According to the regulations, women can only stay in the institute for one year. After one year, they are matched with a spouse."

"What is the method of choosing a spouse? Is there any contact after leaving the institute?"

"There are no specific regulations for choosing a spouse here. Usually, it is introduced by women who have left the institute. After the institute sends someone to investigate and approve, it is done. The women who have left the institute regard this place as their natal family, so they often come and go. Today, there are two people upstairs visiting me." A smile appeared on Ms. Kong's face.

"How is daily management handled?"

"Ah! It is absolutely strict. They cannot receive any outside guests."

By the time the conversation reached this point, the primary school section had already rung the bell for the end of classes. At the same time, the questions seemed to have come to an end, so I stood up and left.

On the way back, I felt as if a sharp stone was pressing on my heart, feeling uneasy for these women who were ostracized from the circle of life.

Although, due to various reasons, I did not go into the women's workplace to observe them in person, the general situation can be inferred from the above conversation under such an environment.

Why can't we have the facilities of a Jiliang Institute ourselves?

I hope that our women's community can pay close attention to this serious question.

Amateur Ramblings

Reality and Phenomenon 262

— Yufu

Reality and phenomenon are two different categories. Reality refers to the objective and actual essence of things that exist. Phenomenon, on the other hand, is what arises from this essence. We often say "social phenomenon," which is not the reality of society, but what is derived from this reality. Every phenomenon necessarily has a certain real foundation; conversely, every reality necessarily gives rise to a certain phenomenon: reality is the mother, phenomenon is the son.

Hegel said, "…but man is not satisfied with merely recognizing phenomena, merely recognizing sensory phenomena. He wants to know what is hidden behind the phenomena, he wants to know what that thing looks like, and he wants to study it. Therefore, we strive to know through thinking that something that is different from itself and the phenomenon, that is, the cause: striving to know the essence that is different from the merely external thing."

Viewing phenomenon and essence as two different categories is Hegel's strength; but his idea that essence is like a soul contained within the phenomenon turns the problem upside down. We know that in physics, there are two categories: essence and phenomenon, but the essence exists objectively, while the phenomenon arises from the essence. Without the essence of the sun, earth, and moon, there would be no phenomena of solar and lunar eclipses. If we shift the problem to social sciences, it is the same. Clearly, there must be the reality of a feudal society or a capitalist society before there can be the phenomena of a feudal society or a capitalist society. It is not the phenomenon of this society that determines its reality, but the reality of this society that produces its phenomena. The problem is that Hegel's view must be reversed to be a scientific explanation.

However, reality and phenomenon are not absolutely different. Under a certain reality, a certain phenomenon will necessarily occur; they are consistent. Ulyanov said, "There is never a fundamental difference between phenomena and the essence of things, and there cannot be such a (fundamental) difference: if there is a difference, it only exists between what is known and what is unknown." This is a true insight. Before we know that electric light and thunder are phenomena that arise from the contact of positive and negative electricity, we certainly will not know the relationship between electric light, thunder, and positive and negative electricity: this is an example of how the difference between essence and phenomenon exists between what is known and what is unknown.

Similarly, in social sciences, a certain social phenomenon must be adapted to a certain reality; there is no fundamental difference between them. For example, the social phenomena of kidnapping, murder, suicide, prostitution, rape, etc., that occur in Shanghai must be consistent with the essence of the real Shanghai society; and the current global economic panic and unemployment crisis are also adapted to the reality of the current capitalist society: these are all very obvious examples.

Therefore, we say that reality and phenomenon are both different and not different: the difference lies in the fact that the phenomenon is the product of reality, reality is the mother, and phenomenon is the son; there is no fundamental difference in that a certain phenomenon necessarily arises from a certain reality, and the phenomenon is consistent with reality, with no fundamental difference.

As for our recognition of reality and grasp of reality, it must be done through phenomenon. Because reality is the foundation, and phenomenon is its product, we can only recognize reality through phenomenon when the phenomenon arising from reality stimulates our senses. For example, our recognition of the reality of capitalist society that has reached the most advanced stage is from the social phenomena of commodity surplus, market shortage, economic panic, unemployment crisis, etc., in this society; we must recognize its reality through these social phenomena, otherwise we will have no way to recognize it.

Social phenomena are very complex and often very contradictory. Clearly, in the current world, on the one hand, there is the promotion of Christian equality and universal love, and on the other hand, there is the social phenomenon of people oppressing people: these are all very contradictory. Therefore, to recognize reality, we cannot observe it from only one aspect, but must recognize the true face of reality through this contradictory phenomenon. Because although these phenomena are contradictory, these contradictory phenomena are all products of reality and are all consistent with reality.

At the same time, society is a whole, and although the phenomena arising from its reality are complex and contradictory, each phenomenon is interconnected. Therefore, we cannot isolate these phenomena and observe them in isolation, but must synthesize them and make a comprehensive study. Only in this way can we recognize reality through phenomenon. Conversely, errors will occur. For example, in the current global economic panic, some industries, such as military industries, have a phenomenon of "prosperity"; if we only observe this phenomenon in isolation and praise the meaning of this "prosperity," then we are wrong, and that cannot be considered recognizing the reality that produces this phenomenon.

In addition, everything is changing, and so are reality and phenomenon, so we should grasp the phenomenon and recognize reality in the midst of change.

Life

Private School Teacher 263

— Shucun

Private school teachers still maintain an important position in the inland provinces today, when "universal education" is only seen on paper. New education has not yet gained widespread belief. Not only are there many cases of setting up private schools in inland villages and towns, but even the high-ranking officials and dignitaries of today often hire teachers to teach in order to improve their children's knowledge of classical learning. In the relatively developed provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, where primary schools are everywhere, many private school teachers have changed their profession to become primary school teachers, but private schools have not completely disappeared. Even in the prosperous Shanghai, which is at the forefront of trends, private schools still exist in poor areas. The author, who likes to study social phenomena, has previously visited teachers who teach children of slum dwellers in Caoshang Nei, West Shanghai, and has also spoken with teachers hired by poor people in Pudong, and has also visited a private school in the countryside of Jiangwan. The number of private schools in Shanghai is so large, not to mention the inland.

In fact, the development of private schools is not only due to need, but there are often cases where a "school" is formed in order to solve the occupational problem of a private school teacher. Private school teachers are intellectuals left over from the old society. These people do not understand the new knowledge. If they do not rely on being proficient in classics, history, poetry, and lyrics, and are hired to set up a school, they would originally be eliminated in this new environment. These people may have had a dazzling and glorious past, but with the progress of the times, they have to step into the path of decline and face the current problem of life. Those who are capable may move to become officials; the next best can draft telegrams and handle literary affairs for dignitaries; those who are worse off have no choice but to be satisfied with being a private school teacher.

Although they are all private school teachers, the teaching labor and treatment are completely different. Among them, the more comfortable and well-paid are those who teach in the families of some important people. The important people treat you as a "teacher" with politeness and consideration. They admire your great name and invite you to come, they have faith in you, and they will never let your annual salary be lower than three hundred to five hundred yuan. In the past, it was not surprising that some officials with great power were willing to spend eighteen hundred yuan a year to hire a "teacher." Now, even a county magistrate or administrative commissioner does not lack the ability to

Page 22

take out about four hundred yuan a year in salary to hire a "scholar" with a solid foundation. In addition to the regular salary, the "teacher" can also get various benefits. If your master is a "popular person" in society or has considerable influence in politics, it is not difficult to get you a "half-official position" as a result of your activity and request. This can be done by "moonlighting" or "receiving a dry salary," or if their young masters and ladies all go to school, they will let you "substantively take over" this position. Over time, you may very well become a prominent official. But this kind of thing is ultimately the most fortunate and rare. Most private school teachers do not have this kind of benefit. Some restrained "old masters" even feel restrained by the master's excessive politeness; if the students are naughty again, they will even "resign" on the pretext. The master often treats them with exquisite food, but they may prefer to enjoy "plain tea and rice"; the master may provide them with some daily necessities such as handkerchiefs and socks, but they prefer to "prepare their own." There are also many such people.

Such private school teachers mostly have a solid foundation in classical learning. Not only are they proficient in classics, history, philosophy, collections, lyrics, songs, and poetry, but they can also write congratulatory messages, obituaries, elegiac couplets, antithetical couplets, and other social articles. Some are also good at official documents and four-six parallel prose with sonorous tones. Their being hired also comes from their works being appreciated. For example, there are quite a few such things now; an official sees a well-written congratulatory message (or lament, or eulogy...) somewhere, and if he likes it, he will ask someone to invite the author to tutor his young master in "national studies." This is accidental, but of course, it is usually introduced by acquaintances or friends.

Originally, there was a difference between "classics schools" and "elementary schools" in private schools. The teachers hired by some important people mentioned above are mostly biased towards the "classics school" aspect of lecturing on classics. What is taught is still nothing more than "classical Chinese" or the Four Books and Five Classics, Zuo Zhuan, etc. Of course, there are also those who teach "national language." In addition, there is also a kind of old master who teaches "classics school." They often regret the "new learning." Parents may have the same view as him, or they may think that classical learning is indispensable in future society. Even if their children have entered junior high school, they still want to take advantage of the opportunity to stuff them into this kind of "classics school" to learn a little classical Chinese and composition. This plan is all for the future to be good at "being an official," and the worse can also be gentlemen and handle writing in the townships. Therefore, there are quite a few "pedantic" gentlemen in the inland now who recruit many disciples from all directions. Although they cannot have "three thousand disciples" like Confucius, it is not a problem to have a dozen or two or thirty outstanding students. In the inland, this kind of school is not worried about not having a place to open. There are ancestral halls, ancestral halls, and public temples or other public residences everywhere. This kind of old master and "university student" can also be inserted in the famous families of "generations of scholars," so this kind of old master is not worried about not having a school.

The annual income of such an "old master" is also very good. Such a "university student," according to their level and family circumstances, must pay the "teacher" from fifteen to forty or fifty yuan in "school fees" each year. Assuming that a "teacher" can teach more than a dozen students, it is not difficult to get three or four hundred yuan. The cost of living in the inland is lower, and this amount may be considerable for them. If they ask questions in society and work as local lawyers, they can even slowly "get rich" (but some stubborn and moral old masters look down on this kind of person).

Finally, I would like to talk about the life of the most miserable kind of private school teacher, the one who teaches "elementary school." The first thing I want to say is their meager treatment. There are those who teach for a whole year with sore throats and get only twenty or thirty yuan. More is no more than seventy or eighty yuan, and it is difficult to exceed one hundred yuan. Farmers are only willing to pay three or four yuan or five or six yuan in tuition each year, and the teacher's students are only a dozen or two children, and the minimum is only seven or eight children, so there will be no more income. There are workers from the Jiangbei gang, the Lianghu gang, the Anhui gang, and the Shandong gang... who hire teachers to come to Shanghai from their local areas. The annual income of this kind of teacher is also difficult to exceed one hundred yuan, so the teachers who teach elementary school are generally poor. But their work is very heavy. They have to manage many stubborn children who do not know a single word, "hold their hands" to teach them to write, and teach many children who are "as stupid as pigs" ten times, a hundred times... but in the end, it is still in vain. If you are not a patient teacher, I guarantee that you will lose your temper a hundred times a day and beat those students until they cry... You often have to shout loudly, shake the "ruler," and put on a terrible face to make some very naughty barefoot children afraid of you... The pain in this kind of life can be said to be "inexpressible."

Technical Interests of Soviet Children 264

— Liangyi

A child in the sixth group of the fifty-ninth school, named Slavo, Roweikov. He has an accurate timetable hanging by his bed at home. It is written like this:

"My Life Timetable"

1. Get up at 7:00 AM and have a good wash (don't forget to brush your teeth).

2. Be sure to do schoolwork.

3. Strengthen my muscles and bones in every way I can (except for wiping shoes).

4. Make an airplane model this summer.

5. Compete in socialism with my father.

6. Do not go to the cinema more than twice in ten days.

7. Be a true Young Pioneer."

That last item has been changed to: "Be a true socialist builder."

The seven rules written by Slavo could have their names signed on them by more than 600,000 citizens of the Soviet Republic over the age of twelve. Indeed, some of them do not make that airplane model, but make a radio or electric motor, and some may not be able to stop themselves from going to the cinema once a day, but the seventh item on this timetable remains the same.

There is also a black-haired, tall child in the sixth group named Koje, Gigs. His limbs are very long, showing sturdy and powerful-looking outside the short sleeves of his shirt; his boots are like a small sapling, coming out of the roof of a dilapidated thatched house.

Gigs is fourteen years old, one year younger than the October Revolution; all he knows about the Tsarist era is from hearsay and books. In those books, there are often many new words that make it difficult for him, many words that he and his companions cannot understand. Gigs deals with those new words by marking them underneath and then satisfying his desire for knowledge in the dictionary later. It is not surprising that he does not understand these words, because they are not only rarely used now, but have also disappeared; so words like "successful people," "preachers," "luck," "His Majesty the Emperor," etc., sound strange and unfamiliar to them.

Once, Gigs saw the word Batman (a military officer's attendant) and said, "What is this?" And after thinking for a while, he gave this conclusion: "Maybe it's someone who plays baseball?"

Gigs' parents are both workers. He and Slavo went to the same school and both belong to the sixth group. In the morning, on a beautiful autumn morning with a chill in the air, the first lesson for the sixth group was gymnastics.

"Are you ready? One, two, three!" the gymnastics teacher shouted.

Light, active, their legs were bouncing on the parallel bars. Their chests were broad, and their muscles were bulging; the large gym was full of light and air. As Slavo grabbed onto the swing frame, he began to whisper to his companion next to him, "Hey! I signed a contract with my father today!

"You're lying."

"Really, I'll show you at recess."

Casual Chatter 265

— Translated by Shui E

Hope is a daytime dream.

No matter how much you scrub pigs, they will still go to the mud.

Except for the heavenly gate, money can enter any door.

Many people, many opinions.

The lazy man's tongue is never lazy.

The hungry, begging for power on the stage, are politicians. The hungry, begging for food on the roadside, are beggars.

"Denial" makes small mistakes become big.

Buy land quickly, marry wives slowly.

A dog that barks from afar will never bite.

If you tie gold to a bird's wings, the bird will never be able to fly in the sky.
